O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and the fullness of the medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of surgery, that is to say "surgery."
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the practice of surgery is forbidden in our region and is completely banned everywhere, the science has perished and disappeared, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors that have been handled by hands (i.e. copied).
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and false beliefs have arisen, and understanding has been closed off and the knowledge has been distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I wish to gather together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will gather together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the explanation and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is diminished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who practices (medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they know precisely the members (of the body), and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of orifices, and the operation and moving and resting veins, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates said that a name without (corresponding) work is much, and in the art of surgery it is little.[ note: this quote means that having knowledge without putting it into practice is not enough, especially in the medical field. ]
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things should be careful not to fall into error and not to kill people; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula in a woman's neck and cut the arteries of her neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took away a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died three days later.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it out, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see one other doctor who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break also had a wound; and the ignorant doctor tightly binds the break over the wound with bandages, and left no cloth on the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg was completely swollen and the foot became lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind his leg; and when I had undone it, he was calm and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in any case, the corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who lanced a boil that had become hardened and then inflamed it due to his lack of skill.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because gangrene, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not at all be touched with iron if the entire corrupt part cannot be completely removed from such a place.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work in which there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take up your weapons in cotton and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best approach so that through the grace of God you may come to safety and be praised; and leave behind dreadful diseases with serious consequences; and put aside your weapons from what causes doubt in you, and have faith in yourself so that you can journey from this world to the other world of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen says in one of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a serious illness, for you will be called a foolish fool."[In other words, it is unwise to attempt to treat a severe or hopeless disease without the proper knowledge and skills, as doing so may result in failure and ridicule.]
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medical caustics, and this chapter is organized from head to toe; it includes the forms of instruments, iron tools for cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter includes the forms of instruments
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about reducing dislocations and sprains, and similar things; it is organized from head to toe and includes the forms of instruments.[3](https://hyp.is/Qr6E0-pWEeyv8k1sXgx4Pw/www.oldfrench-medieval.com/medicine/treatise/traite_de_cirurgie_medievale_extraits.html)
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	In order to remind ourselves of the work, it is necessary for me to describe the qualities of the help and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest to speak of, and a subtle science and hidden knowledge; and of this, many sages have spoken and agreed upon; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I dread the lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally in all constitutions where there is matter, except for two constitutions: namely, the hot constitution without matter, and the dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry constitution together with matter, some have divided and said that cautery is of great help there; and others have said the contrary: that cautery is of no value for disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot and it should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat, nor by dryness; and he who says the contrary says that cautery provides great help for hot and dry disease in the human body.[8]
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And yet, only those who have experienced it and understand through long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of human complexions, as well as the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and seasonal variations should involve themselves with it; we are not afraid of other complexions, even cold and moist ones.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery is among the useful treatments for wounds, and of greater goodness than blistering with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and only affects the member that is burned, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to do so.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Hot medicines spread from member to another and can bring illness with difficult healing, and perhaps even kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its greatness and the goodness of its substance, does not cause this harm unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret which is hidden in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it undoes the sicknesses of bodies, as the philosophers say in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauteries should be performed and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that a cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm that may occur is prevented by the aid of the cautery; and even if the cautery is necessary to alleviate urgent and severe pain that cannot wait for the time when greater harm does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; for there is no return of the disease that is healed by cautery; and they say this; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not only a medicine that changes the complexion, but also dries out the humors that are the cause of pain, and is worth more than other medicines due to its quickness and effectiveness.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness comes to the patient according to their constitution and the location of the disease and its strength; and harmful excesses are gathered in them through the acquisition of foods and similar things, if cauteries are not administered in places where there are little excess and moisture, such as cauteries of dens for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the "last resort" of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cauteries are effective after medical treatments, but their belief is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures in any disease and they are not effective, then we administer cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the belief of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries with instruments of gold are more effective than those of iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. And they said that the location of the cautery does not cause gangrene, but this is not true as I have experienced and found it to be true in some men; and cauteries of gold are more effective than those of iron, just as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it has soon cooled down; and if one heats it too much, they burn it in the fire; and thus there are enough hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to foot, so that the vein may be easier to find.[IS
dou cautere olivaire	The olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is effective for moisture and coldness on the skull, and there are two types that are done for a disease called "soda," and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coldness, such as paralysis and stiffness and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine that clears the head, three or four times, according to what the patient's strength, water content, and habit can tolerate; and then heat up the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands and place their hands on something heavy; after that, put the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and where your middle fingers meet, bleed by making an incision, then heat up the "olivare" cautery, which looks like this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cautery on the mark made with ink, and move your hand downward and outward in small circular motions; then quickly remove your hand, and check to see if you can see a small white spot of bone; and if not, continue applying the cautery until you do see the bone as I have instructed; after that, take a little bit of salt and place it in warm water with soft cotton, and put it on the mark, and leave it there for three days; after that, put wet cotton soaked in butter on top, and leave it on until the heat is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And so said the ancients, that the longer a wound stays open, the more it purges; and therefore, it heals better.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one should let the cautery burn long enough that a part of the bone is burnt, then remove what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others said that one should leave the cautery on for so long and press down so hard that it creates a hole as wide as a finger ring, like the ones women wear in their ears to let out humors; and then one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, it should be cured and bound up.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except for certain people who are in danger; and it seems to me that I should choose the second method; for the wound becomes weakened by continuous discharges due to natural processes, as we have observed in other limbs; and even when the patient's wound is naturally weak, the first cautery seems safer and more effective to me; and with this one, I perform my treatment for a speedy recovery.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of ancient head pain.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes all over the head and lasts long, the patient should use ear drops and pills called "cochie," and purges of the head and eyes and poultices; and if they perform the cautery as we have previously said, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's headache is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly under the cautery that we have mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After this, perform cautery on each temple of the head down to the bone, as we have previously said, and make a cautery at the spot called "vasselz"; it is a place where cups are put; and be gentle with your hand so that you do not go all the way down to the bone: the patient will feel much more pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of that later; and the cauteries at the temples should be finer than those used for the center of the head, and here is the method:
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head sudden pain comes, and the sickness extends to the eye, and the temple is purged with cleansing medicines, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help at all: then cauterization is done in two ways, namely with agury medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of agury medicine is: take a piece of aloe wood, remove the bark and soak it in a little bit of water for two temples, then make an incision in the temple where the pain resides, in such a way that you can place the piece of aloe wood beneath the skin; and when it is placed, bind and hold it tight and leave it like that for twelve hours; then loosen and remove the piece of aloe wood, and let the wound remain like that for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it heals; and if you wish, then use some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is done in this manner: heat the cautery, which has this shape: (image)
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head has the shape of a bell with one curved part, and in the middle there is a small protrusion; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn it slightly, lightly, until half of the thickness of the flesh is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and let there be an abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, place cotton soaked in oil on it, and leave it on for three days; then apply moistened cotton with butter, and then cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this headache with the "cultellare" cautery, at its entire tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	The word "emigraine" in the medieval medical text refers to a type of headache or migraine. It is an archaic term that is no longer used in modern medicine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraines as we have said in the previous division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the previous cautery medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the "cultellare" cautery until it is white; and then gently pass it over the painful area a line half a finger-width long, and remove your hand once, and be careful not to cover the artery and not to reach the bone; and watch out for the jaw which moves when eating, and make sure that the nerve does not move and that spasms do not come to the patient, and watch out for bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear even for those who are unaware and untrained; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it belongs.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is bearable, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautioner that we have mentioned in the chapter on arrow extraction, with the cautioner that has two blades; and this cautioner is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain due to cold dampness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is ear pain due to cold and you have worked on it with solvents and other cures as we have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "pounce" which looks like this:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, puncture all around the affected ear, or both if the pain is in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after marking the incision site; and have ten punctures around each ear; then cure the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	A torture that should be cured by cautery is only one that moves fluids, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this type of torture that moves fluid from sweating and cleanings of the head and gargling, and if it is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third on the jawline between the two lips; and place the cautery on the visible healthy part, and cauterize near the head of the ear a little above and below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a small piece; and leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burned; and this is the method of cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the type of cutting that we have mentioned before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be slightly larger; after curing the wound as I have said before until it heals.[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89tymologie_de_l'expression_%22au_bout_du_tunnel%22)
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient does not have a fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery at the back of the mouth of the stomach; and cure it as we have said before.
de litargie	of diarrhea
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large and pure pills to cleanse the brain; then shave the patient's head and apply the plaster of sinapi, which is written in the treatise on plasters, to the back of their head; and this is the method of cautery: do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If the patient is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, perform three cauteries along the scalp, descending to the neck, with two finger-widths of space between each cautery; treat it as you would other injuries, and if you see fit, add one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns (temples), and continue treatment until they are healed; and use the cautery called "olivare," as I have previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness (or numbness) of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of humors and things previously mentioned; after heating the patient's head, then perform cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, one at the back and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient tolerant, and the illness is severe, perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be for as long as the deepest flesh is burnt, then remove your hand; after that, heal until it is healed, and use the cure called "olivare" that we mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	About epilepsy.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain of humors and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and tolerant of taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, perform gargling and chewing to cleanse the brain frequently with good meats; after heating the head in the middle, then perform one cautery according to what we have said before, and one on the fontanel, and on each temple; and if the patient is severe and tolerant, perform cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and weakness of body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have mentioned.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is young, perform one subtle cautery in the following manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, there are corrupt superfluities or thick phlegm, then apply several cauteries as we have said to the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities are inclined towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them to drink something that will purify the brain, according to what has been previously divided (explained) in the text.[1](footnote-1)
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, anoint the patient's head; then make a well-made linen roll in the shape of a circle and place it on their head, with the patient lying crosswise and held securely from all sides. Then present the liniment and warm it with moderately hot butter from old herbs; then heat the cloth so that the skin can tolerate it. Afterward, remove the circle from inside the head and let it cool down, and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatments until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or, if you wish to cauterize by making several holes with the entire cautery, this method of cauterization moistens the brain greatly. Then place a cotton swab soaked in butter and goose fat on top.[1](footnote-1)
de l’awe des eulz	of the evacuation of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When evacuation first occurs in the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something that purifies the head and guards against all moisture, and make them sweat or take several baths while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, have them tilt their head back, and apply a cautery to the head, and make two cauterizations on the temples if the descent of the evacuation is in both eyes together or in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are underneath the skull, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for blood loss, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incisions, how to stretch them with caution; and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is applied underneath the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids, phlegmatic; then do the cautery that I have said in the beginning descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the eye socket below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three mouthfuls of cooked wine; then raise the head, and do cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and do two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery called "olivary," which has the following form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two pimples as long as they are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the paper is burnt, in the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are performed in two ways: that is, with fire or with a burning medicine.[I have translated "cauteres" as "cauteries" because the word refers to the medical procedure of cauterization.]
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the eyelashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they (the hairs) grow and are even, then place the patient in a upright position; afterward, on a piece of paper place a mark that is similar to the shape of a fern leaf, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered perilla leaves on the eye, then heat up the cautery with the following shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing in the marked shape many times, so that the skin is burned, a sign of the success of the procedure is if you see the paper retracted and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eyelid; then lift your hand and leave it like this for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs return and the paper has softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot as before; and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the paper returns to its natural position and is even, without any hair touching the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fire cautery of medicine is when you instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then take a piece of parchment and shape it like a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and do this quickly so that it does not cool; then spread it on the shaped form as you have made it, like the fern leaf, and place it over the paper of the eyes; if the illness is only in one eye, then work on one side, and if in both, then also; and put cotton soaked in egg white underneath the eye; and the patient's head should be upright and your hand should be pressing on the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, for they will feel a burning sensation as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from its place.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting (of the cautery) has passed, lift the lifting stick and look to see if you see the skin lifted as if it had been lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then place a moistened cotton compress on the burnt area until the burn has cooled. Afterwards, cure the site of the ointment (the burn) called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if it is necessary for you to be vigilant in your work and take great care that no medicine gets into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft (or "mole" in Old French) afterwards, and hairs prick in the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area where the skin has softened properly, just as you did before; after that, cure it until it is healed. This is the form of the leaf of the remedy.[ OPEN AI PROMPT COMPLETIONS MAY BE INACCURATE AND SHOULD ONLY BE USED AS A GUIDE TO WRITING THE FINAL TRANSLATION. ]
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and accordingly you should adjust your constraints (or "constraignemens" in Old French); and do not apply the same strict rules to those who study this art as others.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have a minister hold their head between your hands so that it does not move or leave its position. Afterwards, apply a cotton swab dipped in egg white or parsley juice on the eye. Then heat up the cautery tool which is shaped like a rooster's spur, bring it to the patient's head with the tip of the spur facing forward, and make sure that the cauter is sharpened from one end to the other. Alternatively, you can shape it like a tent, but in any case, ensure that it is sharp enough for your task.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove any pus or dry matter from it. If it is closed, then open it up and remove the blockage. Then place hot bran on top of the cautery tool, and hold your hand with the cautery to the white part near the eye, but be careful not to move your hand excessively. Next, apply the cautery tool to the fatty tissue around the eye and allow it to corrupt (i.e. burn).
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you reach the bone at the beginning of cauterization, that would be good. If not, then perform cautery again and continue to do so as needed, leaving it for three days. Afterwards, place a cotton swab dipped in butter on top of the eye, and treat the inflammation with a drying agent until it is healed. If 40 days have passed and it is still not healed, then apply a corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and proceed according to what comes in its chapter (i.e. continue treatment as necessary).
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a kind of fire cautery for abscesses that some of the ancients mentioned. et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the size of a thumb's width; and hold your hand firmly on the probe, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and it is necessary to put a wet cotton swab dipped in egg white or rose water on the patient's eye: the lead will draw out the pus from the abscess, and the healthy flesh will heal miraculously.

And if the abscess is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. de la dolor des dens	of toothache

des scrophules	of scrofula (a disease affecting the lymphatic glands in the neck).

dou cautere de pleuresin	Of pleurisy cautery.

The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy using aristolochia roots, and in the following manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the area that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining slightly backwards; and one cautery at the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the breast away from the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make it open as if you were smelling something.

de la menoison	of the operation/treatment

de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions but to no avail, then perform cauterizations: three on the spine at the base, one of which is located directly below the lower back and triangular-shaped, and one cauterization below the belly button. Two should be done.[translated text](https://drive.google.com/file/d/1RgLQjyX246bYlJvT0GnG3K_Z79fqrBHw/view?usp=sharing)
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled down, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then give him a large cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the area covered by the cauterization; and leave the cautery in place for a long time. Afterwards, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy part which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul", heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, then place it completely aflame on the cut "thelul"; and leave your hand in that position until the cauter reaches the opening of the vein, from where the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there are many "theluls", cauterize each one as we have said; then cure them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchemy, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the work of a cutter or surgeon, which we will discuss later, then comes such illness that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone, and it is festering and casting putrefied matter and corrupt humors, you should probe it with a thin probe and make sure that you know the depth of the probe entirely. Afterward, heat the cautery which looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and continue heating the cautery until the corrupted flesh and humors are burnt, one time, or two or three times, according to the amount needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are there, and the great veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestines, beware of those areas, and do not make it outside except in a fleshy place, and consider that it is not persistent; after curing the place until it is healed, and if the place is scarred, and the materials have been removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is rotten, and the bones at the bottom are corrupted; and similarly to one of those that we will discuss later.
de la maladie des reins	Here is a possible continuation of the text about kidney disease:
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the kidneys comes from cold or from a large amount of gas and he does not desire a woman, then you should make cautery on both sides of the kidneys with the clavicle cautery that we mentioned before; and if we perform the cauterization in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, which will provide greater help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform a fire cautery on the outside part above the bladder, where the hair of the groin begins, with one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the width of a coin; and perform one cautery on the back, or two if necessary; and let the cauteries be made with a hot iron according to the previous description.
