Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and it does not allow for proper conception to occur, and the menses are corrupt and come late; and when they do come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to perform three cauteries around the belly, as we have described in the fire cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the back; and let the cauteries be made with a hot iron, as previously described.
de la hainche	It appears that the word "hainche" is not present in the provided text. Please check the spelling of the word or provide more context for me to better understand what you are asking for.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When moist humors descend to the hip's case, and for this reason, it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the joint's departure is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip's case with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the location around the case so that the case is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain in the hip.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip's case, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division, but the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills or other similar good-working pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, perform cauterization; and the types of cauterization are according to two methods: that is to say, hot medicinal applications, and fire cauterization. Fire cauterization is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the cyst of the abscess three triangular cauters according to this form, and make a deep and large wound between each cauter, the size of two fingers, and let the cauters be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cauter is performed in the middle on the top of the abscess, so that there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, you can cauterize with the circular cauter that we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the abscess; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire abscess, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used for sciatica, when pain occurs in the hip but does not reach down to the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauters are performed where the patient indicates that the pain resides, and one cauer at the ankle four fingers wide on the left side; and let the cauters be knife-shaped, and burn the thickest parts of the flesh; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the bones of the foot or near it, then cauterize where the pain is felt with three or four points using the cauter called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, more are performed; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a knife-shaped or circular cauter is performed, and be careful in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cauter on for too long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who have done cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and the foot as well, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. After a belly wound from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, do cautery in one and the other, following this method. // And the wise men said in the cauterization of inflammation, of which this is the manner, make an iron like a needle of dactyl (a unit of measurement), or just a bit smaller, and let it be interlaced, and let there be space between the interlacings equivalent to the width of a nut; and let the interlacings be turned two ways, and let them also be like knots, and there should be one well-made iron handle; and this is its form.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is all red and starts to drip, then place it on the swelling of the affected boil, and turn it over on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery point, leaving it for three days; then make a poultice of butter and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and yet it is one of the good cauteries that can endure it, where it affects.[*I have translated 'regard' as 'appearance', as I believe Al-Zahrawi was referring to the scary appearance of cautery which might be the reason why people were hesitant to use it.*]
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or being struck, or from excessive evacuation, or from an expansion of cold matter, no form of cauterization is effective for these instances, except for that which results from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar treatments, three lines be signed on the back, in the area where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line there should be five cauterizations or more, depending on the severity and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterization be done using the type called "poins"; and if you wish, do three or four cauterizations at the middle clavicle following this form:[Image](https://i.imgur.com/EZKWw4h.png)
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the spine, at the base of the back, a swelling which appears above the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it using the "celcle" type of cautery, following this form:[Image](https://i.imgur.com/EZKWw4h.png)
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine equally. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine using the cautery, making two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another. Afterwards, cure the area until it is healed, as we have said, and take care not to apply cautery to a gouty area that is in a nerve span.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture that has spread to every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which is called "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it should be treated with cautery in the following way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to cauterize the sole of the foot, then make a single cautery that covers the whole area called "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which happens often, then make three or four cauteries on each knee on all sides, with the cautery being olive-shaped; and if you need more, then do so, but do not keep your hand there for too long that the thickness of the flesh is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and have them take medicines. Because if you provide good care for them and purge phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the nature of syphilis
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When syphilis comes with fever, and the bowels descend to the anus and it is recent, then when you see to cure it, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that the feces descend from their stomach. Afterward, make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the boil subsides, and press gently with your fingers around the syphilis above the bone of the wrist, and in a straight line above the body; then heat the cautery, the shape of which is as follows:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	...until it turns white and expels pus. Then press the bowels back to their place, and have the caregiver hold their hand so that they do not move back again. Provide good support for the patient's legs, and place a cushion and a servant under each thigh and another on the chest who holds the patient's hands. Place the cautery on the mark with your entire hand, holding it firmly and continuing to apply pressure until you reach the bone. If you do not reach the bone the first time, continue trying again until you do so. Be careful not to cause the boil to burst or burn the patient excessively, and take care that they do not die or suffer further harm as a result of this procedure.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be fine according to the measure of eggs, and also large for big people according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is removed; after curing with other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the boils do not come out when he takes a walk in chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him, and carry it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he works little and guards himself from excessive consumption of drink and food, and from too loud laughing; and when he follows this instruction, he will be fully healed. And I will speak later about the cure of surgery in its chapter.

But the first cauterization is lighter and more nimble.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb, either from falling or injury, and this pain lasts for a long time and medical treatment is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "pointed" cauterizing iron, and let the cauterization be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and virtue, and its location of twists and pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that is good; if not, begin another cauterization on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is near it, so you must do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cauterization with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from the putrefaction of humors and melancholy. When do you see it necessary to cauterize, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient's body, then perform five cauterizations on the head: one on the crown, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cauter reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out, allowing the vapors of the thick humors to escape; and cauterize the area according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the affliction is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the knees of the hips, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the lower back; and sometimes do cauterization on the bone of the wrist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cauterization you do, the more help you provide, and it benefits them; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary for cauteries to be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the manner of irons. Afterwards cure the place with a mixture of bran flour and honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	I believe you are asking for a translation of the word "enfleure." The term is not used in the given medieval medical text, but I will provide a translation regardless.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines, oils, and plasters, yet it is not healed, then cautery is done on the limb according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep in the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the opening of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but never should anyone intervene if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the openings of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	I am not certain what you are asking for. The term "de albaras" does not appear in the Old French medical text provided earlier. Could you please clarify your request or provide additional context? I would be happy to help once I understand better what you are looking for.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become advanced and the means of medicine are of no avail, then cauterize it with a cautery that is moderately deep, according to the size of the flesh, until the swelling disappears and the color changes; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and the blood of a chicken and a pigeon, each in equal parts; and mix everything together and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to the air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	Here is a possible translation of "li cure de chancre par cautere" from Old French:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre begins to appear, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that has the shape of a circle, all around the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, with the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot grow (or develop)
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it delays in developing, either because of the excess it makes or due to the water in the sick person when they are very old (that is, too old) and have little blood, or for time; and you wish to hasten its development: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards, leave it like that. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it (the diseased part) entirely with the cautery, heat the cautery until it is in the shape of this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the core, and such that the cauteries are felt from the outside in such a way that the course of the gangrene is alleviated. Afterward heal it until it has perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire with iron/metal
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of illness is called "corrodens," which is nothing but an eating away of the limbs, just like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cauterization with heat, then slowly heat up the pointed and large cauteries according to where the illness is located; afterwards, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, so that nothing remains of it. Then let it be for three days, and apply crushed herbs with oil on the burnt areas until the burns from the fire are healed, along with all the corruption. Afterward, cure it with ointments that generate flesh. And if after three days you see that healthy flesh is not born, that's good; but if not, then repeat the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted places. And this eating away has sometimes been cured by a soothing medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already spoken about the cure of the soothing medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the corn(s) that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Very often, a disease arises in the feet, which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large swelling that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this disease is of two kinds: namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is as follows: heat a cauterizing iron as thin as a pen nib, made of good metal, so that it can touch the swelling on all sides, with fine edges; then place it very hot on the swelling, and keep your hand turned tightly around the swelling until it reaches the base of the swelling; and leave it in place for three days until it begins to putrefy; then apply a plaster made of crushed mallow with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the swelling will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound with a cleansing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by moisture in the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in the following way: take a rod of iron or copper, or a pen nib, and place the clot or althelul (that is, powdered verrucae) on the clot; then place the rod on top so that it heats up all around, then add some hot water, and hold your hand tightly, pressing down while turning so that the edges of the rod come into contact with the root of the clot, and can find a path through to the root; and allow the patient to endure the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it in place, and it will detach all by itself along with its roots. Do this repeatedly until you have cauterized all of those on the body, then cure the wounds with ointments that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for tremors.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold nerves or quartan fever or another cause, you should apply four or five cauteries to the spine, one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the chest, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes, abnormal swellings or stinking pustules that come from corrupted matter appear on the body. In such cases, it is necessary to perform cauterization on each pustule's head as soon as they appear using a fine cauterizing iron made from myrtle wood, with the tip heated in fire, or a long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cauterizing iron. At times, these pustules are cauterized at the beginning in this manner, and they cannot grow any further; instead, the excess matter that causes them is ruptured and healed. However, it is important that this be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut[translate.google.com](https://translate.google.com)
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is a large flow of blood from an artery that is cut in the wound or incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things. And it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, you should quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press down very hard so that the blood is calmed down under your finger and no more drips out; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both small and large, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, depending on the wound and the location where the artery is cut, to the vein where you have placed your finger and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another one quickly from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and take care not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is through one of the four ways we have mentioned: through cautery, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will manage the stopping of the bleeding by tightly binding it with bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it.[Reference(s):
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone and they do not have any remedy or medicine, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it stops bleeding above the wound and above the vein; and they should not move it, but apply cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations in advance for what they need of cauteries and medicines.[Reference(s):
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgeries.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and have described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on head injuries at the beginning up to the feet, and in this chapter I will follow the same path so that one can more easily find what one desires.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is important for you to know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake foolish things. For many types of people come to be treated, some of whom are so afflicted by their illness that they easily die from the violence they find in their disease and the severity of their suffering; and one should fear for such people.  [](Note: The text contains several spelling variations and archaic forms that do not affect the meaning.)
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these, there are some who claim to be healed and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the disease is deceitful. It is not at all appropriate to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not rashly but skillfully open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you establish a good reputation, and glory, and lasting praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have organized this chapter for you, dividing it into sections according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have described from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a swollen head filled with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the womb grasps the child's head too forcefully; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason that we know of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death hastened; and therefore it seems to me that it is better for me to leave off working on such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and it became heavier each day until he could no longer support it; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture accumulates under the bone at the top of the spine, between the throat and the bone; and the operation is such if the moisture is between the throat and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the head a finger-width long, so that the moisture can run out; and here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are the earlaps of the head opening up on each side, and fluid comes out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not heal: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision, remove all the moisture; after removing it, bind the incisions with cloth and powder, and put vinegar and oil on it, and leave it like that until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and continue to bind the head as well, and give the patient dry food without much moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to make an incision is to look for the size of the abscess and where the pus has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, make the incision where the abscess is visible and where the pus has gathered, in a way that is appropriate for what you are able to do; and be careful not to cut an artery; and if blood flows out, then the patient will die from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rupture/injury
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or the fissure, and the illness is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help at all, then the last cure is the cautery with this, that one will burn two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you burn the eyes, it is necessary that the patient bend their head back; then they rub the area around the eyes with a rough cloth until the arteries appear; then the patient tightens their neck with a single cloth; then look where the veins are blue, and the locations of one and the other are next to the ears, and they are sunken; then mark the locations with ink, then burn one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be along the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see an artery, place the spatula underneath it and burn above it, cutting as two fingers crosswise.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is burned, blood will continuously spurt out.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not open to the touch, you should measure a quantity of three fingers' width, then make an incision down to the bone; and the amount of blood that needs to be let is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can tolerate and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the surface of the bone, cut away any abscesses that have formed, then close the wound and bind it, treating it with a dressing until it heals.
de emigrainne	I would be happy to help you translate "de emigrainne" from Old French into English. However, I must point out that "emigrainne" is not a recognizable term in Old French. It's possible that there may be a spelling error or missing context for the term.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and there is a cough, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples, swelling of the head and similar things, and it is treated with various medical cures but none are effective, we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for extracting them is as follows: the patient should shave their temples and pay attention to the artery that they can feel beating in the temple, for it beats quite noticeably and is rarely not visible except in some men who are too cold; and if the artery is hidden, have the patient strain their neck with a cloth, then apply rough fabric to the area and pour warm water over it until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take a spatula of the following shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up using hemostats, and carefully separate it from the membranes that are beneath it on each side; and if the arteries are fine, then hook them with the tip of a dissector probe, then cut that part according to the size of the two holes. For if it is not cut, the blood will not exit properly in its entirety.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from the six holes, up to three; and if the artery is large, then it should be tied in two places with a sturdy double thread of silk, so that putrefaction does not occur before the wound heals, and proper bleeding occurs; then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the area with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the holes are closed; and this is the more difficult task, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cautery helps to end moisture (excess fluid): therefore it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In which case, for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and apply well-made bandages; and when they are removed, cure the area with dry medicines that promote healing, and keep applying bandages until it has healed; and if a piece of the artery remains as long as you work on it, then quickly close the opening with cautery or use vitriol in the wound and apply pressure to stop the bleeding; and if this is not available, place your finger over the wound until the blood coagulates, and continue applying cold water until it stops; and the more difficult and lighter method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the incision with this sharp cautery on both sides, but make sure the edge is thick enough to maintain its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and when you have marked the two places, place the red-hot iron on it until it reaches the bone and cut the vein in two places; and they should be far apart because this cautery is not welded together in its entirety; such is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears come from the veins that are above the forehead and no medical treatment helps, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsating sensation on the forehead like a shiver; and if the eyelids are closed and moist such that the paper has fallen off, and the paper is heated up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And this remedy was called "cure contuse" by the ancients, and it consists of shaving the hair from the forehead of the patient who has this illness, then making three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to the length of the forehead. One of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, going down to the eyebrows, while the other two are at the temples above the eyelids. Be careful not to cut the arteries that are located near the temples, and keep your hand away from the jaw bones. Each wound should be the length of three fingers joined together.[ST1]
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth to wipe away the blood, then apply the following mixture, made from two parts of:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is above the temple to the second incision; and remove the skin that is between the two cuts, all the way to the syfac that is on the bone, then do the same thing from the middle incision to the other second incision, and finally remove this mixture.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	insert into the first incision the instrument called "cultellaria," which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other. Here is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place the sharp edge of the costotome towards the fleshy part of the skin and the blunt side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. Cut all the veins that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to where the skin can be seen. Then do the same thing in the middle incision down to the other second incision; and then remove the blood equally on both sides, squeezing out any excess blood; then place a piece of old cotton gauze in each incision, cover it with wet cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar, and make sure no pus forms. On the third day, untie the bandage and apply a large amount of cold water, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment and rose oil, as well as other cures used for wounds, until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting a catarrh, and you see the eyes sunken and small, with weakened vision, and burning paper; and their hair falls out, and they have deep pain in their head, and the patient coughs; then know by these symptoms that those matters and those catarrhs do not come from one vein alone, and the cure for it is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you shall command the patient to lean their forehead back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another of about one inch. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let it be up to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the incision and put old cotton in between, and use linen bandages; then bind wet cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and be careful to avoid hot abscesses; once removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, and then cure it with drying agents that promote tissue growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make it into a plaster; and apply it on these wounds to promote tissue growth throughout.[note: Colophony is a resin obtained from pine trees, used as an ointment base or for waterproofing. It was also used in medicine.]
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or animals, or minerals such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something falls into the ear, such as a stone or other object that does not adhere to or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then facilitate extraction; and make them sneeze using a condiment, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward. Often, this cure will cause it to come out; and if it does not come out, facilitate extraction using delicate pincers, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a fine hook made of thin wire; and if it does not come out this way, make a tin tube and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that no air can enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, as often it will come out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take glue (such as used to catch birds) and place some on an instrument made for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with any of the things we have mentioned, then quickly make an incision in the ear so that pus and hardened matter come out, and spasms; and the manner of making the incision is as follows: first make the patient bleed from the head by opening a vein and extracting blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands with their ear facing upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear in the fatty tissue or where it is swollen; and let the incision be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck out the pus with your mouth; treat it until it heals.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and becomes swollen, perform an extraction; and if it cannot come out, apply a thin probe according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision on the grain. But do not do so when you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with delicate pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Therefore, in the water that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing of condiments first and widen the ear with soft cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out through this, it's good. If not, take many small and light stones, heat them a little by the fire, and put one or two of them in the patient's ear and jump on one foot on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop striking stone by stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out completely. And if you see, take a reed, and put one end of it in the ear, and light the other end with fire until the larger part of the reed is burned; then repeat this with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then apply extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the treatment is not beneficial, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then pull them out with fine forceps, and if you don't see any, then take a probe of the kind described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow below and wide above. Insert the slender end of the probe into the ear according to the severity of the patient's discomfort, then push the entire probe; do this frequently until all the worms come out. If they do not obey by coming out, then stop up the probe with cotton as I have said in the previous text. And if they still do not come out as we have mentioned, then administer the distillations that the ancients have tested in the treatment of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, in the manner that you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or bronze, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation. For pressing the distillation inside, use a well-made bronze instrument for that purpose. If you choose to take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip, then pour your oil or juice and what you wish of your medicines into the probe. The probe should be in the ear. Then insert the scraper with all the cotton, and press gently until the oil is distilled or reaches the ear canal. Have the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a small amount heated by fire so that it can be distilled into the ear. Take care that it is not too cold because the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	"de l'estoupement des oreilles" means "of stopping up ears" in English.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	A child is born who has no hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults from blockage due to wound or pus inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small bump instead of a hole, and one can see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that goes deep and cannot be seen is of difficult healing in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, work on it immediately with this instrument, as described in the following form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the obstruction is from pus or flesh of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers, and cut it lightly until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the obstruction is deep in the ear, take a delicate, light razor, heat it slightly by the fire, and then place it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the obstruction when the patient complains of discomfort or pain in hearing, make a small incision carefully, making sure not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert a wick into the hole according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder on top of broken vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then heal it until it is clean.
