Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of paper scraps/shavings.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eyebright that comes in paper when the eyes are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and forceps, and cut a little bit of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not cut out, cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and after the incision, the cauterizer must move; and many times they heal, as long as something remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, those roots are burnt and do not return.
de la gresle	Of hail or a hailstone. The term "gresle" in Old French can refer to a hailstone or hail in general. It is a natural weather phenomenon where ice pellets or stones fall from the sky during a storm, often causing damage to crops, buildings, and animals.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come to the paper of the eyes certain things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "gravel" (or "hail"), and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: observe whether the gravel moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision on each side, then gently peel back the skin on both sides, then take it with forceps, and cut it. If you cannot cover it without puncturing the paper a little, do not worry about causing harm to the patient; and if the tear is large, stitch it together, and care for it until it heals; and if it is small, do nothing at all, because the ointments quickly restore it and help the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel is descending inside the ear toward the upper part, then turn over the paper (skin) and extend the gravel with forceps, and cut it and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, do not worry about it; and when the gravel is cut out, rinse the eye with salty water, and cure the wound of what harms the flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that has been spread on paper sheets, and this happens more often in children than in others, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they get "catharre" in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie down on their faces and sleep, and their papers under their eyebrows are moist, which causes swelling and changes the appearance of the exinach that is apparent in the eye. And when you press the area around it with your fingers, you can feel the exinach coming out.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the treatment is as follows: the patient places their head over your sanctioned area; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach comes together in the center; then make an incision in the middle of the moist area, as wide as the cut made during bloodletting from a vein; and insert the knife deep enough until you reach the exinach; and in several ways, the exinach comes out of the incision, in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it all in one piece with a piece of cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and make sure not to press too hard on the incision, nor come all the way through with the knife to the eye, so as not to wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not appear at the beginning of the cut, slightly increase the cut lengthwise until it becomes visible; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place them on the wound, and bind it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that has remained; then cure it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the place, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs (or fibers) of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs (or fibers) other than those that are natural grow and become ingrown, they harm the eyes and cause various illnesses such as excessive tearing and swelling of the eyelids and cataracts, to the point of causing eye destruction. And there are four ways to cure it: either with a cautery made of fire, or with medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cautery, and this can be done through incision and suturing or by applying bandages, depending on what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle with a thread on it; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow near the hairs, and pull the thread over the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, to the full extent, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then lay on the paper a figure of a pin, such as a myrtle leaf, and nonetheless it is necessary that the figure corresponds to the height that you wish to raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to cut a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make an incision to the full extent along the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the large tear duct down to the small one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs, as thick as a root, then insert the probe into one of the two angles of the eye, and scrape it all; then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a needle with a single thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the superfluity of the threads dry on the eyebrows with some sticky substances, if you wish to do so; and if not, then pay no attention, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without drying or constraining things, as the paper will swell at the healing of the wound and bring it together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients have said), and this work is done without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it is in another way, then mark the paper with a figure that looks like a myrtle leaf, as we have told, with three incisions separated according to the shape that is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut what protrudes with small forces equally according to the shape that is shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the power to hold the pincers and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread and place it in the middle of the wound; put one thread next to the large notch, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have told; then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a compress and similar calming ointment.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the wound become embedded: in this case, you should do as we have said about incisions, but stitches in one and the other are more refined.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of ulcers is as follows: you should turn the skin and make two incisions in the manner that I have said, and then make two subtle sutures as long as the skin and as wide as the space between them; and cut off the two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; then bring the two ends together gently over the upper part of the skin of the eye, and pull the two sutures tightly from both sides; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin that has been pulled will die and become necrotic and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it does not heal, then cut deeper and cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has healed and the skin rises up again, and the hairs no longer prick, this is the shape of the two sutures that you will make according to this figure, and according to the length and width shown.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine strand of silk; then align the edges and tie them together gently, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length; then prepare another fine strand of silken thread and tie its ends; then place the patient's head in your lap; and make sure it is in a sunny spot so that the work can be clearly seen, for it is delicate and fine work; then insert the needle into the entire chase at the root of the adjusted hair, and quickly pierce through the paper up to the natural hair; then pull out the hairs right up to the chase, and insert the pulled-out hairs into the chase, if there are one or two or three or more; then pull your hand away so that all the hairs come out at the chase on the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is pierced and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the chase down below where you have placed the thread, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you can see it with your eyes; then you will pull the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hairs harden in their place and the scab forms; and if the hairs are small, then attach one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and raise it along with that or leave it alone, until it has become detached and then lift it up.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eye's decay.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or decay occurs in the eye, it can happen in two ways: one naturally, and the other unnaturally. It can suddenly occur due to a wound, a cut, or a cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of the treatment is that you split that suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying and constricting substances in the cure of it. Because if you do so, the illness will return worse than before; but use soothing substances, such as fenugreek; and let water agar or althea and flaxseed be cooked, and let heated oils of diaculon be poured into one of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and cure it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is to take heed that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and these treatments that we have mentioned are nothing but corrections for this illness, so that it does not return to the shape that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is under the eye is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural as well as accidental. The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way to work on it is that you take a needle, with two threads on it, and stick it in the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come into two parts of the flesh; then stretch the skin above all the needle, and cut it at one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the form of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a knife and place it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits along the edge inside the paper; and let the corners of the two slits be the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make them so that when they are assembled, the form is like the form of a letter called "j greek"; then remove the flesh according to the width that its edges are below, of what follows the paper, then join the two severed parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said of soothing medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a wound or stitch or cautery, it is necessary that you make an incision in the form of a clean line below the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare means by all their power to make the form return to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is required in terms of labor and instruments, in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bonding happens to many people in such a way that the paper is bonded with the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a knife beneath the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers, so as to cut the very thin membrane that is not raw, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient can bear it without the knife being too sharp and harming the eye; and let your incision, with which you flay this assembly, be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and let the whole of this assembly be healed, and at times put in the eye salty water, and wash it with clear water and collyrium; then place between the paper and the eye a bandage of linen, and place on the eye wet wool in abundance of egg; and after three days use collyrium and other healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the toe of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the toe (ungle) comes in two forms: it is either nervous and similar to a hard callus, or not nervous but rather resembles congealed white mucus. When one touches it with iron and attempts to pinch it, nothing can be done; and one form or the other begins near the large tear duct (grant larmier) and grows little by little until it covers the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your lap, then you open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand and use tweezers to pull the toe (ungle) upwards; stretch it over a small piece of leather and place it on top. Then take a needle, put a horsehair, cow hair, or buffalo hair through it along with strong thread, bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the toe. Pass the entire needle through and tie the toe with thread, stretching it over the leather. Then skin the side of the toe that follows the vein and artery (prunele) down to the bulb (soie) of the hair, all the way to the head, leaving only the cartilage or tear duct intact so that tears do not flow through the incision as usual. Sometimes the toe is stretched to the bone (oncine) with thread, as we have said; then one skins it gently, removing all of the thin membrane (spatumile), which looks like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the thin membrane (spatumile) does not touch the fleshy cloth and break, and that the vein (prunele) is not pierced; after the incision, put a little bit of crushed salt and collyrium made from litharge into the eye and leave it until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this similar condition of a nail is often cured with medical methods; and they come to be like I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye look and take the spatula smoothly, not too sharp, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully file the nail, and if you see that it is becoming thinner and the swelling approaches, distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red lead and oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then lactate it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid night in the eye causes great harm, then suspend it with a suture and remove a part of it but not all, so that there is no flow of tears; then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Sometimes a red flesh grows over the pupil in some men's eyes, covering the pupil and turning it upwards, appearing like a baluster rose; and the procedure is that the patient puts his head into your hands, then you open their eyes, and remove all that flesh with suitable tweezers, holding it firmly; then cut the first layer of flesh, continuing to cut until the end, making sure not to wound the eye in the process; and let the incision be made with a spatula as we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and small forceps used to remove splinters, as shown in the following form in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then apply a mixture of rose oil or you can distillate collyrium red and similar corrosive medicines to the eye; place cotton with egg white on the eye outside so that it is secured from hot abscess; if anything remains, and pus accumulates and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with calming agents; then return to your work until the eye has healed, and do this each time flesh grows back in the eye in such a manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary to lighten the treatment for each weak eye of natural disposition; and in case of accidental disposition, through iron work; and do not insert your hand into any of these procedures until you see that this limb can withstand the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that are covered over the eye and take away from its function, weakening the eye all days. Therefore, it is necessary first to look at the eye and see if there is only sebel (a type of inflammation), and not another illness; then, treat the eye in this way: command the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently pull those veins to the very end according to your judgment, and let the pulling be subtle double in this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two strings/ligaments in one piece following this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, carefully pull those veins with force, and wipe the blood away hour by hour, until you see that the veins move outside of the eye; and take care not to poke the eye with the tips of the spatulas (medical instruments), and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as not to miss those veins; and once you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to dissolve what remains of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster (medical dressing) for the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and is certain of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method which is before until it heals; and this is the form of the treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The experts call "arissati" a fistula: when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it that you should lance on the abscess, where it should burst, and drain all the pus in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then use all the instruments described in the following form; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron with one sharp end, and pointed like a file as in this form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the iron on the corrupt bone, then turn it between your hands and press lightly until you feel that the corruption has been removed; and do this several times, then apply drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is healed and flesh has grown, and the wound of the bow is closed, and remains so for 40 days without being renewed or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, then know that it is healed; if not, there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: which is to uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with hot medicine, and when it is exposed, take a gimlet of this form, and let the iron be in three angles, and the rod be tapered up to the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye by about a finger width, then turn the entire stylet until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of breathing if they hold their hand on their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened, the matter will go to the nose; this makes it an easier task for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide all around and there is no discharge or decrease in size, then bind the patient; then clean it, then apply suction cups or a haterel without striking, then place a bandage made of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye, and then compress the eye and dress it with linen bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount of material needed for the eye; then bind it tightly with a strong bandage, and reapply the suction cups without striking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the bandage softens, tighten it again; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good; if not, reapply the dressing and cloths and bandage until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the rupture of a round loaf of bread.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the outer coat (pupil), then it opens, and comes out like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see; if you see such a thing, the procedure is as follows: insert a needle to the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the eyelid; and make it pass through, leaving the first needle in place according to its position; then cut the loose end of the doubled thread and tie one part of the eye around, and bind it tightly, then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth soaked in egg white on top; and leave it until the film sticks to the eye, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is bandaged with a cloth strip all around the eye until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a great appearance (swelling), then pierce it with a fine stylet that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor flow out and make the eye descend, and enter quickly; then remove it until it heals.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyebow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a swelling gathered in the eye, appearing like water descending, and it is not water; and one of the ways to recognize this condition is as follows: have the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then hold their head with both hands, and move it so that you see the swelling come above your eyes; then insert (a probe) and let the light not descend or fall, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not go down, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not arranged as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine stylet and press on the cornea through the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling goes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or boiled water with fenugreek and honey, into the eye; and let it be cured with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similar cases of waters (or fluids) in division, and what is necessary to pierce through; and we work accordingly, depending on the health (of the eye). It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light by the sun, and hold the healthy eye very tightly shut; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the tip of the instrument named "almagda" next to the crown by the thickness of a hair in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument named "almagda" strongly, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel when almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is to the depth of the measure from the pupil to the end of the darkness (or color); and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horned canvas, and then put the instrument until it reaches where the water is, and then press it under a path after another. If the water comes out now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the water rises again along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and no longer rises, gently remove almagda by turning your hand slowly; then put in a little bit of gemstone salt, and raise the eye inside. Then place over it cotton or damp wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye. We (I), and those who are of our time, place common bread broth with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then perforate the joint only, and do not go too deep, but make a shallow incision, then apply cautery, as we have said; and at the completion of the procedure, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which they sleep on their back in a dark room; and be devoid of all movements, and partake light meals, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate to perform this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If abscesses come to a head, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed down, then unbind the vision and place on his face one bandage to cover for some days, and always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house a little at a time, and gradually return to your usual activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in their country they make a type of cautery called "almagda" which one sucks the water out of, but yet I never saw any such thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see them; and they should be made of pure copper:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same delicacy, and their buttocks have three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from (off) the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes diverse fleshy growths appear on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are those that have a swelling of fox-colored flesh, while others have soft flesh of good color. In the case of this type of flesh that is soft and not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils and apply the lancet to those growths and pull them out; then cut what you can hold onto with a sharp spatula on one side, until you are certain that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut, open it with a very sharp and light instrument so that nothing is left; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, cauterize them quickly to stop the bleeding and remove all of the flesh; then pour vinegar or warm water on the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose does not open and moisture reaches the palate, you should know that it is healed; but if the moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is new flesh grown in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut. In this case, you should insert a moderately thick linen thread and tie it with your hands so that there is a space of about one digit between each knot; then place the thread in the patient's nose as far as possible and pull it out while sniffing until it comes through the nose into the mouth. Children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing to do. Then hold the part that comes through the nose with one hand and the part that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and feel your way along the knots in the thread. Do this until you are certain that the knots have rotted the flesh; then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all of the remaining flesh; and then place a piece of linen cloth in the nose for several days until it is healed. If it is necessary to use drying medicines, do so. This is the form of the instrument used to cleanse the head, as oil and medicine are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, such as a candle, and its conduit is similar; and if you wish, make a closed canal, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, a disease arises in the head of the nose that is called "telul," and it grows and becomes large to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you must lance it at the beginning and remove all of it, then place the cautery or heated medicine on top; and if you delay lancing it until it has become large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, with poor sensation: do not touch it at all with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is lanced even once, great harm can come to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that you can completely lance it, then empty the patient and perform the lancing without fear, and cure the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is lanced and sutured[ ](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/quant%20li%20neis%20est%20copez%20et%20cosus)
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must cauterize all the edges of them until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a suture and bind them, and put dragon's blood powder and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or another plaster that adheres on it, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men, hard abscesses like peas, smaller and larger, appear within the lips. Then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each lump, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply the place after the incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped; and then leave it open to air, and cure the place of dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swollen flesh arises on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with forceps and cut its root, and let the pus or blood run; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, hard and rough shells gather at the base of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, which are unsightly; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, and greenish, such that corruption reaches the gum, causing bad breath; it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and clean the teeth or shells until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what comes out at the first scraping, that is good; otherwise, repeat the process on the second and third day, until everything is removed; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments to be cleaned, depending on what the work requires, because the rasps used to clean outside the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; and have these forms and others prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure teeth, it is necessary to delay pulling them as much as possible, because this should not be done hastily; for it is a very important substance until there is no excuse for scraping (or removing the tooth).
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is ready to pull, you should make sure of the decayed tooth. Often it happens that the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not leave, because the abscess remains, as we have often seen with surgeons. And when you are certain of the decayed tooth, you should cauterize all around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum on all sides; then pull it with your hands or with delicate tweezers firmly at first and then more gently, until it is well loosened; then securely fasten the tweezers; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is cracked and decayed, you must fill it with pieces of cloth where the cracks are; and carefully fasten it with tweezers so that it does not break when tightening; and one must work very delicately around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not break it and leave a part in, which would cause greater pain for the patient due to the malice of the root. Be careful not to act as ignorant surgeons sometimes do, who out of haste and recklessness sometimes break the jawbone and do not provide what is needed; but instead bring about great sickness from the remaining roots or from the broken jawbone, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, or salt water; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to move teeth should have long and thick handles that do not bend when pulling out the tooth. And these are the forms (of the instruments):
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be made of strong iron, and let them have teeth to hold sutures.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling, you should place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on the spot for one or two days until the place softens, then use forceps called "algefri", which resemble the beak of a bird; and inside let them be made like a file, and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all of these forceps, then you must cut open the flesh all around the root, and place in it an instrument called "althali", that is to say, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:[img](https://i.imgur.com/vN6PnF0.png)
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots come out with this, that is good; if not, then use all of the instruments, of which the shapes are shown hereafter:[img](https://i.imgur.com/YtQ9VxM.png)[I'm glad I could help you translate the medieval medical text! If you have any other questions or need further assistance, just let me know. Imgur links for images of the instruments mentioned in the last two lines can be found above.]
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps themselves with this instrument which has two branches, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other metal tools which are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong enough that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental tools; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned here. The wise master will find his own instrument according to what his work and the disease shows him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any tool because of their diversity. And if one breaks a tooth or another bone, they should search among the tools that I have mentioned and help themselves with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy enough to hold the bone so that it does not break, but can hold and extract it. And then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, one should heal it with all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is not erupted in a straight position, and it cannot be pulled or filed: then remove it; but if it is loose with the other tooth, take this instrument, the shape of which is shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take the pliers in your hands for several days due to the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file like this, the shape of which is shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is similar to the files used for making needles; and file down the tooth little by little every day, so that it does not move until it falls out; then use a smooth plane at the end for everything, and if the tooth is too sharp and injures the tongue, you should file down its roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or harm speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen in front, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success, then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth (if there are one or more) between the loose teeth, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from the part where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers, align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, so that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it tightly in place as long as it can endure, and if it loosens or the wire breaks, then constrict it with another wire; if it remains in place, it will serve thus all its time, and this is the method for aligning teeth and realigning two loose teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place immediately, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled interfere, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the wire of the tongue.
