Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is a ligament under the tongue that is natural and present at birth, or it can occur due to an accident of a healed wound. The procedure is as follows: you open the patient's mouth, have their head in your lap, and lift the tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment. If there is hardness or knot, it is due to the healing of a wound, then use a hook and cut the ligament widely. Be careful not to cut too deep, as the artery is located beneath it. Once you have finished, apply warm rose water and eau de laxative or cold water under the tongue, then place a linen tent under the tongue. The patient should wear this every night so that the wound does not heal. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol and if it continues to bleed, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this. Then continue treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then throw the "oncine" on it, and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood overcomes your work, then put vinegar powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the limb gently and leave it to be healed, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come within the throat growths that are called "godath," and they are properly referred to as "the two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be cautious: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and bluish color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it at all with iron, for fear of bleeding; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will break on its own; and if it is of a white color and has fine roots, then have your instruments ready to cover, but first look to see if the hard swelling is at rest and calm. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and let his chin be in your lap, and have the servant open the mouth and take the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue down beneath the entire instrument, of which this is the method; and it should be of silver or fine brass, just like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue down beneath this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the "oncine" and insert it into the almond, and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, of which this is the method, which resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are curved towards each other, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool at hand, then take pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner; and after the incision, rinse the patient's throat with warm water, and water and vinegar, and if bleeding occurs, rinse the patient's throat with water, or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them then in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely one of small size; and it had completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was stopped up, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for one day or two. And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two pieces through the two nostrils. I therefore acted quickly and inserted a probe into one of them; then I pulled it out and drained a large amount of pus; then I did the same thing in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut off a piece of it, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled the space that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I squeezed it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it no longer grew; and I left those parts without knowing what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape (from Latin "uva") or from Old French "ueil, oeil" meaning egg. Without more context, it is difficult to determine which one is intended in this case.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye". Once it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is thin, then it is necessary to make an incision; and the one that is round assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a fuscous color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision on it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you must have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and make an incision with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it heals. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a ruse with cauterization without fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp pointed. And it is that the patient places their head on your healthy part, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and apply live steam, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the steam from this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a hair on the head where one applies the medicine, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie down on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and cause choking; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour, until you see it reddened and the bites of the medicine have calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with the cotton all the way into the corner above, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to start the cautery of the medicine again, then do so, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with a swab wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put a spout on it, and boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the eyes be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes mortified; then restart it often, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and never do it except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to overwhelm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or a fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what you cannot see and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit after the food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come up through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, then take an instrument of plastic of this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and have the head raised up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, so that he does not choke or push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient himself inserts the instrument, so that he knows where the object is located; and let him insert it downwards, or pull it out completely with the entire instrument until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the swelling of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the tonsils are medicined, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the tonsil, then pull it with a tiny hook, or with delicate tweezers that are suitable for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a piece of chewed rope, and put it in the sick person's throat, then put a hot iron on the end of the rope and do this often. And if the sick person becomes hoarse all day, then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the tonsil feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, then fumigate the sick person with asafetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall out without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a perforated cloth, and the hole of the instrument should be in this opening; then put your fumigation in, and the sick person should put the end of the rope in their mouth, and close their mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but reaches the tonsil; and the tonsil will fall out now, and if it does not fall out, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the sick person suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to pull out the tonsil is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers that can enter the throat; and it resembles a surgeon's beak, and has roughness like sandpaper, so that what it grasps, it cannot release; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what the memory brings hereafter of one and the other in this book; and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its likeness itself, and those that hold moisture. And the second way is for the locations where they are in the body. For abscesses of the head are different than those of the base, and abscesses of the fleshy part are different than those that come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, by which it causes contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the base, so one should pierce it while it is still alive; and it is not appropriate to pierce a grown abscess without completed digestion, except for those that are near the base, so that it does not rot inside and form a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the incision in the lower part of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and on all sides where there is no cavity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And in those that swell, according to the member. And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better to leave the incision until it is firm in completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body of it will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member requires. And in small abscesses, make small incisions; and in large abscesses, make large incisions, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where you must sew the core and cover it; when it has become as a piece of cloth, and is dead, it is necessary to do as one does with boils; and some abscesses are cut in three angles, and some have cuts like the leaf of myrtle, such as angina abscesses; and there are those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce it; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, do not pull out all the pus in that hour, but pull out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then pull out something more; do this many times, bit by bit, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak virtue, such as women, small children, old and decrepit men. For the spirit sometimes jumps when the pus comes out, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not notice. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe away the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, then apply linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many holes, then it is necessary to put in a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of the skin in the abscess and turned it over, then it is necessary to fill it with old linen cloth or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold and clear water, and moisten a cloth, and place it on the bleeding site multiple times. And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, lightly applied. And if this is in winter, and the location where the abscess is is very sensitive, then you must put tents and wet cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is in summer, and the location is fleshy, then you must place damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said. And then loosen the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be generally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is this chapter.
des soros	"des soros" likely refers to "abscesses" or "swellings." The term comes from Latin "sors," meaning a lot or drawing of lots. In medical contexts, it referred to the pus-filled swelling that forms when a part of the body is infected.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where small abscesses of the head come, and they are of two kinds, as the joints of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty and such where there is moisture like pustules; and some are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not contradict. And the work of cutting consists of trying every one instrument that is called "entromissoire", of which the form comes after, what thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, so you pierce above the long [one]. And when the moisture has been drained, so skin without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again if anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will cure this. And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you are sure that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound with suitable ointment, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds a hard core, so cut it lengthwise; and throw your sutures there, and skin it all around, and put all your effort into drawing out the cyst where it lies; and if the artery contradicts you, so do what I told you after. And similarly do for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And some of these abscesses on the head or where there is no moisture, and one of those abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and found the abscess as a hard, rough and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had struck it, they would have made as much wound as with a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those that come to children's heads and roots of ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that pus can exit easily; and cure them as is necessary.
des scrophules	The term "scrophules" refers to a type of abscess or swelling that was commonly found in the lymph nodes of the neck. In medieval medical texts, scrophules were often associated with tuberculosis and other chronic infectious diseases. Treatment for scrophules typically involved surgery to drain the pus and abscesses, as well as the use of various ointments, salves, and other remedies to promote healing and prevent infection. The term "scrofula" is derived from the Latin word "scrofa," meaning "female pig," possibly because the swollen lymph nodes resembled the swelling of a pig's neck glands.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Scrophules often occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in other areas of the body, and are connected to each other. Each scrofula is specifically located within its own cavity, as we have described with neck abscesses and head abscesses. The similarities of these scrophules are many. Some contain moisture, while others are malignant and do not want to obey health. In that one you see with good disposition, and has the color of the skin, and moves easily from each side, and is not swollen in the nerves of the neck or in the artery or conduit, and is not deep; so it should be cut open from above, and skinned on all sides, and pull the two lips of the wound with sutures if necessary, as we have said about head abscesses; and drain the pus bit by bit, and make sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and the scalpel should not be sharp or cutting, so that little is left behind, and does not go too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder or any drying powders in the wound, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skill if there remain any small scrofulous lumps, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, do not cut this scrofula at its root, but bind it with a double strong thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it up, making sure there is no excess flesh due to the size of the scrofula. You must focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sew it as we have said. For those scrofulas that have excess flesh, pierce them where it appears necessary; and pierce them as described earlier, by hanging, then apply dressings with oil and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a healing ointment until it heals.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" in Old French can be translated to modern English as "of sciatica". Sciatica is a type of pain that affects the sciatic nerve, which runs from the lower back down to the legs.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the operation of cutting the throat, but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is according to their writings.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglotte" be cleared; and this is not done with help, because all the veins and the patient's windpipe are blocked by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two amygdales.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid suffocation caused by constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to incise the epiglotte, it is necessary that we make the incision under three or four circles or a small cut crosswise between the two or three circles, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are suitable for the incision of the epiglotte because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long and narrow.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the windpipe; and let out the vessels of blood, if you see any, and then cut the syfac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that jumps out at the opening where it is broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed during which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the windpipe wound and sew it up without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote tissue growth until it is healed.[
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely choked up and the patient is judged to be at the point of death, and the breath no longer audible.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then place a bite on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus they are kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and this occurs in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw (or have seen).
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting part of the tendons in the neck.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure it, and found it as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew for certain that it had not received medical attention nor been properly treated except for the throat, and breath was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, treating it until it healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing further happened to the young lady than that she was hoarse from screaming, and later regained her health.[STHAP
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in the operation on the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a lentil, and it is common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is of two types: natural and accidental; the natural one has no malice (evil intention).
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is of two kinds, one similar to fat, and the other kind similar to an abscess that comes from an artery.[IT] Et la premiere maniere est appellee «hernie de graisse», et si est engendree par exces de graisse qui va a une des gorges;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not at all suitable to operate with fire on a small one, and test and examine the entire probe:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like an inflamed gland and it is not responsive to any vein, then cut it as one would cut a nail, pulling out its entire root if there is one.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search thoroughly around and treat it as appropriate until it is fully healed.
des nous	of the nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways (kinds) are there, which I will tell you all the similarities of;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary that I tell you all the difference that is between nou(t) and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever holding, until the ebullition has passed, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With nou(t) there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains 1 suppuration (sfac), which is its own sack and according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and becomes big;[.](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/.i.)
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and there are two similarities (kinds), either fatty or moist, and many colors as I have said in the division.[Note: The word "division" here likely refers to a section of the text where different types of issues were classified and described.]
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the care of the nose, that you first test and examine the instrument called "entromissoire" according to its shape as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry for abscesses of the nose is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess and turn your fingers back and forth until you are sure that the instrument has penetrated the core, according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the entromissoire and take care that nothing falls out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs clear, with whatever color it has, let it drain as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is fat; then drain it in the shape of a cross and take hold of it with forceps, and lightly skin it from each side and place a bandage where it lies so you can remove the nose whole along with the abscess.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pain will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if some of it remains and the blood bothers you, then apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind the wound, place calming hot compresses on the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.[9]
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound and treat the one that contains decaying flesh.[10][11]
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is constricted or if something else is opposing you, then hasten and apply vitriol powder to it, leaving it there for two or three days until the wound rots and the boiling of the blood subsides; then return to covering what remains of the new wound.[12][13]
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of invasive instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three corners which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses or fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are similar to the needles used to sew surgeries, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and they are proven to be better for encircling the hollows of fistulas using black lead.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And they are of three types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.[Reference(s):
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the hooks are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and some hooks have two hollows of three types as well.[Reference(s):
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are some who have three humps, and they are also of three kinds; and there are some who have two humps, and others who have only one hump, and they are also of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these [humps/growths] are sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, so as to skin the nails, in order that the vein or nerve is not cut.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these instruments are the alemelles (a type of surgical instrument) attached to handles, so that the patient does not realize their use during the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use it except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and ankles, and similar locations;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes a small instrument, resembling the scabs of abscesses, in this shape, to staunch blood;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one places it sometimes in the wound that bleeds profusely from the veins and arteries, and sometimes in this large shape;[Answer 3 (12th-13th century Old French text):]
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupt, so much so that they resemble the breasts of a woman;[Answer 4 (12th-13th century Old French text):]
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them should proceed according to this form of the line b to g:[Answer 5 (12th-13th century Old French text):]
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine using lard, then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sinks downwards and is softened due to its size, as it often happens in women, then make two cuts on it in a similar fashion (to the first cuts);
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	such that one is connected to the other at the end of each, in a way that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this shape, from this line (line b) to line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two sides (of the cut), and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, as well as everything necessary for healing, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to a loss of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive onion.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it rots away the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it becomes healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come in the armpits are types of hard scrofulas, some of which contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be lanced in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all of the cotton, and cure it with an appropriate ointment until it becomes healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like the form of scrofula, lance them as we have said in cuts for scrofula, and if the wound turns hollow, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin over it is stuck, it often results in abscesses, and the same happens when the vein is swollen and abscessed;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And one can recognize it as such when it is due to an artery, for the abscess is long and deep;[IST] et por ce doit on traitier l’aposteme de l’artere en tel maniere.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, there is a pulling sensation; and when it is due to a vein, it is a visible swelling;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the nails, near the joints, at the neck, and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one must avoid the iron treatment, and also in case of an abscess at the head, and for one that is swollen from an engorged artery, make a incision on top of the skin.[----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make the incision like an "oncia" (a unit of weight and volume used in ancient apothecary), and carefully separate the artery from the surrounding tissue, until it is fully exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle underneath it and make it pass through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the location that is between the two joints of an instrument until the pus inside it comes out, and let the abscess be relieved;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment to heal the wound, until the blood clots.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat that with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is due to an incision in the vein, then you should apply your hand and press on the abscess all the way to the skin,[ST1]
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then insert the needle under the location you are holding with your hand, and make it penetrate, and have a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, with a ligature of one of the two parts to the two ends of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you fear that the thread may come loose, insert another needle under each thread throughout the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads tight in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut away the excess of the core and leave what is tied;[tex:
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a damp cloth on it with wine and oil, then provide care with bandages and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses can come in the artery and vein, and abscesses can also come to the nerves when they are wounded or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all places where there are joints, and this is a severe abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and it is in various forms without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when (the abscess) is strongly constricted, the patient feels pain, and it is not deeply in the body, but beneath the chest.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it can move in all directions but does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and the one who is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for by chance there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is at the head or forehead, makes the skin (or flesh) split with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut into its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a string, and then lance and cut it out, then stitch the wound closed and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there appear in the belly and not elsewhere blisters, and it is a disease called "funge" by its likeness, and it has thin roots, and large abscesses; and there are small ones and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two in his belly that resembled funge more than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were split open, and moisture flowed from them continuously.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found one to weigh eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces, and the appearance in the incision is such that you can tell if the patient is moist, and the color of the flesh is white and moist with fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	And cut it with a wide spatula, and have the cautery ready with fire in your presence. For when cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then quickly cauterize.[Reference(s):
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision of iron, take a well-made piece of flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	Then hold it (the thread) tight and do not stop tightening the flax thread until the artery is cut through and this happens without difficulty; and if the roots are thick, there is a risk of cutting the belly as well, but you can still manage to cut only half (of the artery).
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	After that, cauterize (the artery) so that it does not come back to life; then treat the wound and make sure not to cut the vein which is of a foxy color and poor sensation and has a milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a swelling comes from a cautery of a wound or a crack in a syphilitic sore, and it is on the abdomen and in the vicinity of some of the intestines, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is described above, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to the rupture of the syphilitic sore and the protrusion of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when pressed with one's fingers, it recedes, and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly enlarges at the entrance to the bath and after heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing, and it is clearly apparent when pressed with one's hand, and does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a certain quantity,
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, it is easy to touch, and the procedure is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you should leave the treatment. Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or a swelling, you should instruct the patient to expose their throat and lie completely flat, then tie a bandage all around the swelling;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then command them to lie still between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go around the place you have designated for the entire duration of the treatment,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch out half of the abscess above with a large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk tightly, and leave some slack in the tie.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open up half of the abscess that is stretched out on the thread and insert your index finger, and search for the intestines.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught in the thread, then untie it, and push the intestine back into the abdomen;[INTEGER] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find pus, then take hold of it with the hook, and cut away the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein resists you, then go around it and then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have created in a cross that you made to pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then constrict the abscess in four stages around the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area alone until it dries up, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or cut it when it has become thin and rotten, then treat what needs to be treated and cure the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as needed, and close the wound.[
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have mentioned in the division the similarities of chancre and how it should be treated with medicines and how to avoid iron treatment. And we say that chancre worsens in the marrow, and great caution is required in its treatment. The ancients said that when chancres are in a place where they can be scraped, such as chancres on breasts, thighs, and similar places, it should all be removed when it first appears. And when it has grown and become old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never healed any from it; nor did anyone heal it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The procedure, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have mentioned, is to first purge the patient of black bile once; then make them sweat if they show clear signs of indigestion. Then prepare the patient for the procedure by providing a comfortable place for them. Next, throw your instruments onto the chancre and remove all hair from around it without leaving any behind. Let the blood flow freely and press the area with your hand or some object until bleeding stops completely. If the natural course of bleeding is contrary to incisions on the artery or vein, cauterize the area until the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with other remedies until it heals completely.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
