Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and relaxation of the belly and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and they have no other illness but dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this way:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient up with your hands, and have the assistant press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula according to this form: And let it be sharpened on two parts to a point, but in no way should it be so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and it should not be able to bleed;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look to see if the dropsy has descended towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the belly three fingers wide and straight below the navel; and if the dropsy is due to illness of the liver, let your incision be on the left side of the belly three fingers wide; and if it is due to the spleen, let it be on the right, and it is important that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to this weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce through all the skin with the instrument and insert it, and lift your hand to keep the spatula between the skin and the abscess as in flaying, up to the length of a fingernail or thereabouts; then pierce the abscess until the spatula reaches the visible place, and this is the place of the water, then pull it out and insert this instrument of which this is the form: And it resembles a slender silver cane, and is made of light iron or copper, and has a small hole in the lower part; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other, and one on the other; and the incision is cut like a feather quill, and this is the form of the incision that writers make with a pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	upon the head is the Adam's apple, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it then subsides onto the tool; empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient may die due to the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the amount of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength indicate, and his pulses; then pull the tool and hold the water, and it is now held back by the muscle that stops the passage which is above the syphac, which I have spoken of, that you pierce in this manner; then resume the tool the next day, if you see the patient enduring this, and draw a small amount of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this for some days, and be careful not to overdo it until only a little water remains. And if you have doubts about the patient, and leave too much water, then cure him with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and let him drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the blockage of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes a child is born without an opening in the foreskin, or the opening is small or not in its proper place. In such cases, it is necessary to make a tiny incision of one spatulam very delicately following this form: then place a thin plug of linen in the opening and keep it tied and in place for three or four days. When he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, then replace the plug; and perhaps it is not even necessary, because the urine that comes out will not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	The one whose opening is small can be treated with a linen plug as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are wounded, because some are born with the opening at the head of the foreskin, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the tip, and this is a serious disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of this procedure is as follows: the patient lies on his back, then stretches out the head of the penis and holds it in a position like the width of a pen, so that the opening is in the middle as it should be; and be careful not to allow any bleeding which often occurs, and if it does occur, stop it with a styptic and cure the wound until it has healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these ulcers come to the penis, and it is a foul appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and benign ones; so one should take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean all of it, then put a cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and discharge, one should apply cautery to it. When you have cut it out, and if the ulcer is in the middle of the penis, and has part of it under the skin and part outside, one must remove the ulcer that is under the skin first; and when it is healed, then cure the exterior part. Because when cured together, the head of the penis is not secure, and there will be perforation, and blackness and corruption on its penis and in the groin; so one must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour from the rind of pomegranates and vinegar, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, one should apply lunar cautery in the following manner: The cautery helps with two conditions together, that is, bloodletting and corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then one must insert a reed of wood into the penis for the patient to urinate through it. And when the skin at the head of the penis has been washed clean (which occurs in those who are not circumcised), or by wound or abscess, one must then scrape it with an instrument called "cheveit," until the foreskin is loosened and freed from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is difficult to cut, then one must scrape it with a "spatumile" (a half-round spatula or knife) on the head of the penis and foreskin; then carefully separate between the two, and place a thin piece of linen cloth soaked in cold water, but not washing again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as cutting open a continuation like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this work of our own volition, and particularly on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that the majority of masters and healers who performed circumcision used a lancet, and forceps, and a scalpel; the ligament is avoided because there are two layers of skin, and by chance one might cut the upper layer and leave the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the foreskin is not completely removed, and the pain is doubled, and during the cleansing with a lancet, there is no certainty that the tip of the member will be clean; and during the cleansing of the nail by chance the iron might slip, and they ruin the work, and often it happens that there is no need for cleansing, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification that is done to the sutures of all the seam, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces (needles) cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, you cut evenly in one continuous motion; but the thread should be tightly wrapped around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if they pay attention, that you are only tying the thread around the member, and then you cheer them up in all the ways you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then hold the penis straight between your hands and place the needles between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them or any of the instruments; then put your hand on the member and blow and pull up until the head of the penis is out; then clean it well of any collected filth, then bind the wound with a double thread, then bind it underneath with one tie to another tie; and hold it with two fingers by the second tie at the pocket and thumb, and cut between the two ties, then quickly lift the foreskin and pull the head of the penis out.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let a little blood flow, for this is the merody (medicinal bleeding); and put powder on it and on the powder a cloth dipped in a half of an egg white tempered with rose water, combined with good and fresh red oil, and leave it on until the next day, and continue to treat it until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The procedure for purging is as follows: let the two ends (of the instrument) be even and sharp, and let them be of equal length as the blade.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purging is when the heart retreats at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the place becomes abscessed; and cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it (the patient) survives for three days, and what is beneath the groin is swollen, then leave it alone until the abscess has subsided, and then gently skin it; cut it as much as you can move it, and be careful not to harm the area of the groin, it will not be harmed at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the wound with a dry abscess by applying powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut too deeply into the heart and it goes above (the intended location), it will not be harmed; then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	about holding in urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, coagulated blood, pus, flesh born dead, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division;

des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or corruption has gathered there, and you wish to distill water and medicine into it, then make use of an instrument called a "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the hairy place where the medicinal plug should be such that it stops the vessel well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push in when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see fit to insert your medicines into the bladder, place the tip of the syringe in the moisture, and pull on the drawstring that is on it; by pulling the drawstring, you will draw the moisture into the syringe, and then firmly push the drawstring back in; the moisture will enter, and will now reach the bladder, so that the patient will feel it.

And if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly all around; then put a strong string through these holes, then assemble the circle like one assembles a bucket, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the kinds of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and I have told you the difference between the stone engendered in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work with cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates painfully, and urinates frequently, and then becomes constipated; and there is much leaping of the foundation; and the healing is light for children until they are 4 years old, but heavy in the elderly, and it is moderate for those in middle age, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, one must first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it often hinders in searching for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and straighten them out, moving them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out at times; then make him sit between your hands, prepared, and have his hands beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely lowered; then search for and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut into the stone. And if it does not fall at the touch of the whole (stone), moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is a mature adolescent; and insert it into their rectum, searching for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it up to the neck of the bladder; then press on it with your finger and push it out where you see that you can cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press on the bladder with his hand, and order him to lift up the hips with his right hand, and with his left hand move aside the skin that is under the hips in the place where the incision is made; then insert the spatula, which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make an incision between what is between the haunches and the anus, not in the middle but next to the left thigh; and let it be straight on the stone, and your hands should be always at the anus or the stone, and let the cut of the incision be wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Perhaps the pressure from the hands at the anus will make it come out without effort; and know that some stones have angles and edges, making them difficult to extract; and there are some that are smooth and round, similar to a gallstone, where the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To the one then who has angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must use pincers that are like a file at the tip to carefully extract the stone so that it does not break; or insert under it an instrument with a thin curved tip; and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, widen the wound slightly and if the tissue swells, constrict it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, insert first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above it and pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, it must be sawn, and a larger wound must be made. For two things can happen to the patient: either they die or urine comes continuously so that the wound cannot heal; but in any case try to extract it, or break it up with pincers, until you pull it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then turn the patient towards you on their side, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then clean it with a fine salve and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot abscesses or corrosions come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, causing urine retention, manifested by pain when urinating: then insert your finger into the wound and extract the clotted blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then raise the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help it heal in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary to bind the patient's thighs together and apply medicine to the area each time you treat them.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the bladder is small, and it is located in the conduit of the rod, and is pierced and fixed inside, and the urine cannot come out; so cure it as I say, that you cut it many times, it is excused from being cut for this cure. I have proven this already.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a fork of iron in this form and let it be fixed with three prongs in one stick:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take a thread and tie it around the rod under the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the fork gently into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork with your hand in the hole of the stone, until you can pierce through the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod. It will quickly break apart and exit along with the urine, and the patient will be healed.[Notes: This passage seems to describe a procedure for removing a bladder stone by inserting a fork-shaped instrument into the urethra, breaking the stone, and allowing it to pass through the urethra with the urine. The described method is similar to lithotomy, an ancient surgical practice of removing bladder stones.]
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because of some obstruction, then tie a thread under the stone and another above it; then make an incision in the rod next to the stone between the two ties; then extract it and untie the string, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; treat the wound until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women (i.e., a kidney stone or gallstone)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is passed by women, and if it does occur, the cure is difficult and is forbidden by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skillful woman who will reveal herself to the midwives, even when she is honest.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skillful woman in this art of midwifery; and the fourth manner is that the stone of women is often more deeply embedded than the stone of men, for which reason it requires a deeper incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, one should urge the following: you must find a skilled midwife, but they are hard to come by. If you cannot find one, then at least find an honest and subtle virgin midwife. Present her with a bowl of water and have her examine the woman's life, or have a woman who knows part of the art do so. Then command her to perform the examination for the stone as you have instructed.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And carefully check if the woman is a virgin: if so, insert your finger into her rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, press downwards under her groin and instruct her to push down with her hand and press hard on her bladder with her left hand.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, she must slowly move it from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then place a stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is easiest to feel, and press the stone in that spot; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make the incision initially shallow.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	and then push the rod into the incision, if you feel the stone increase the wound size so that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, with corners. So know their appearances to recognize the exit.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if blood overcomes you, put alum powder on the wound and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the tools with you that I mentioned in the extraction of stones in humans to help you with your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if blood overcomes you, and it is an artery that has been cut, put the powder on the wound and hold it in place with bandages and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, because the patient may die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has calmed down and the area has healed, return to your work, until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	Of a carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquose is nothing but a gathering of moisture or white humor, which is beneath the skin of the groin, and contains the egg (testicle); and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin between the white humor that we have mentioned; and these do not happen if there is no swelling.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of this ramice is due to weakness in the groin, and this material spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it is caused by a blow to the groin, and this moisture can have many different colors: it can be yellowish in color, or not reddish, or black, or whitish-blue, and there are more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white pus like we mentioned, then the abscess is ripe, that is, a long lump like an egg's shape, and the corners are not visible, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the very skin, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and because of this, it is thought to be another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the corners and the white pus, then it can be felt well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, squeeze it with the quadratic instrument, with which it was formed in front.[NOTE: I'm assuming "li forme est ci devant" means "it was formed in front", as in using an instrument on it. If there is more context to suggest otherwise, please let me know]
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside based on what comes after the instrument.[NOTE: I'm assuming "ceu" refers to "the moisture". If there is more context to suggest otherwise, please let me know]
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then place them on their back, on something a bit elevated, and put many rags underneath them;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then have them sit on their left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on their right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the loins;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the scalpel and cut the skin of the loins lengthwise along it down to the small of the back, and make your incision straight through the skin of the loins until you reach the white linea alba, and carefully flay the skin according to your ability;

et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg (referring to the rounded head of the femur) jumps out of place during your work, put it back in its place once you have completed the operation on the hip; then bring the two leaves of the kidney membrane together with one stitch, then cure it like the other wounds until it is healed.

et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ramic is used as a fire cautery instead of an iron knife, and that is to take a scalpel-like cautery, and cut the skin of the buttocks, and heat it up as we have said, so that the white pus containing water is exposed;

et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if any thing is against it, such as an abscess or bleeding or other things, cure what is against it, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then use perforation as I told you, that is when you are certain through the signs we have mentioned that the ramic aquous (a type of herb) is ready.

puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then place cotton on the wound and bind it, allowing the remaining liquid to drain out, and continue to care for it until the wound heals.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the wound's mouth, then you should put in a feather or the instrument used to treat the water from edematous patients, of which the form is described above; and widen one spot of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is gathered after 6 months or thereabouts, and when it is gathered as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the haunches (buttocks)
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this abscess, there is fear in many ways, so it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.[Comment: In this context, "work" means the treatment or cure for the abscess and "similarities" refers to other medical conditions that are similar to the abscess.]
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come about in the body, and also in the joints; and this is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It should be known that this is caused by an excess of acrid and sharp humors, which are spread to the joints through impact.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; and it is not painful, and it is a severe abscess.[Notes: I am assuming that "grievous" or "severe" is meant here since the text says that such an abscess is not painful. The French word used is "grief," which can mean both "painful" and "serious" depending on context.]
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And perhaps it is an abscess that is grievous, fearsome, and putrid, of a dark color; and sometimes it comes from a burst artery or swelling of the vein.

de la routure dou syfac	"of the surgical incision on the abscess" or "of the cutting open of the abscess"
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The event of this branch (of the arteriae iliaca) is due to the section that comes from the syphac (the abscess in the groin), or the extension on the stomach in the side of the haunches, due to which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the hips.

de hernie carnouse	for a carnosus hernia[^1^](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/carnosus)
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this section, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment using iron/metal.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made in such a way as the branch that is connected to the vine, in a manner that you bind the vessels, gently after the incision below it.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dip in it, and treat the abscess of the one working on it, until the pus comes out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes there comes a rupture in the intestines, as we have said, and the opening becomes apparent; and none of the intestines come out at the hips, and if any do come out, it is little by little, and heals every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	nevertheless, if it remains in that state for too long, the wound or hernia grows larger, until the intestines come out;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens due to the extension of the hernia in the groin, as we have said. et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the pus that is under the skin, then take a rag and place it on the visible surface of the abscess;
