Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syfilis (syfac) is constricted and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is more appropriate in this place and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the buttocks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the fat inside is liquefied and it is visible; and when one wants to cure it, it is necessary to make the patient lie on their stomach, and then cut the softened skin on the natural skin; then bring the two lips together with a suture, and if you see, first sew up the excess of softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds until it is healed and the thread falls out.
dou chastrement	Of castration.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is so that the physician knows how to answer when asked about it and how to cure it; and the other because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and other beasts. So I say that castration is done in two ways: either by attrition or by cutting. In the one we do by attrition, we make the animal sit in hot water until the genitals are softened and hanging; then pull them with your hand until they retract and you no longer feel them. Regarding castration by cutting: it is necessary to tie up the animal, and press the skin of the genitals with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each testicle once, when you have well skinned them; and leave some of the soft tissue and fine tissue that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is better than the one done by attrition because in attrition there may be a remnant of the genitals left, due to which the animal still desires lust; then cure the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two kinds for men: one is when between the two hips there is an opening as in the shape of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes urine flows. And the other kind is for women, with a bulge like a man's virile member and two hips. And the treatment for both sexes is to cut away the fused parts and cure them like other wounds. In the second kind of men, when urine shoots through the skin of the hips, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	"tentigine" does not appear in the given text. It is possible that it was a typo and the correct term is "tetigene", which means "that which can be touched or felt". However, without more context, it's difficult to provide an accurate translation.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a growth that attaches to the natural parts, and it is too unsightly to see; some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment: You must bind the excess of the tentigine to your hand or with bandages, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, for fear of causing bleeding. After curing one wound, move on to another growth that arises at the mouth of the marris (possibly a type of skin lesion), and use it, and perhaps it will heal on its own, and it resembles a cow's udder, and because of this, it was called by the ancients "cow disease." It must be cut in the same way as we have said for tentigine, and cured until it is healed.
de erratique	of something erratic or prone to dislocation
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	An erratic condition exists when the nature of a woman is not functioning properly, or the opening is small; this can be natural at birth or caused by disease; or it may result from a tight ligature, or subtle and fine syphilis, which has penetrated deep into the matrix, on the sides, below, or elsewhere. This prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes even menstruation. The recognition of this condition is through the observation of the belly. If the obstruction is visible, then use your fingers or a probe. If it is subtle syphilis and located near the two lips, then act quickly: place your two index fingers together, with the woman lying on her back, legs spread apart; then stretch the two lips widely apart, so that the subtle syphilis is exposed and lies over the obstruction. Then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on top of the obstruction. The woman should have sexual intercourse every day, so that it does not heal. If the syphilis is hard and thick, then use a spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf. If the obstruction is made of thick flesh, then suspend it with a needle and cut it; and use hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then insert a wide horn or tube so that the wound does not heal; this should be done for a long time, until it is cured. If flesh has grown in the matrix, then cut it according to this method, unless there are large abscesses. For an enlarged abscess in the matrix, do not touch it with any instrument.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids: "des" is a contraction of "de les", meaning "of the", and "emorroides" refers to swollen veins in the rectum or anus.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are enlarged veins that are not usually visible but become so over time, and when they become old, they turn into a type of growth called "thelul". We have already discussed the similarities and signs of hemorrhoids earlier, and now I will mention those that can be treated. Hemorrhoids and "thelul" that are inside the rectum or anus and not visible to touch cannot be cured with surgery. Those that are at the opening of the rectum can be felt and therefore cured. It is necessary to place the woman in a cool room, then use pincers to pull out the hemorrhoids by their roots, then apply powdered medicines that constrict blood flow, such as acacia and dragon's blood, and similar things. Then let her stand with her back against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water. If bleeding occurs, place her in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peel, galls, and similar things. Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg yolk, and make a plaster to apply on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, then apply cups to the back and breasts without breaking the skin; then take wool, moisten it in plantain or cleaver juice with old wine, and heat it on the area. Once the swelling has subsided, cure the wound with ointment until it heals. The one called "albathir" is red and looks like a rough surface, it should be treated as mentioned for hemorrhoids and cured until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses on the groin
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the groin, such as chancre, abscesses filled with pus, herpes, ecthyma, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, as well as other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that burst on their own; and if you wish to know about the operation with fire, look and see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if you can see it. Then, do not rush to pierce, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and place two small seats where they can lean back, and support their back and stretch out their legs past the thigh; and let their hips be spread apart, and place their arms beneath their knees, and bind them well with a good ligament; then turn them towards the right side, and prepare the instrument used to open the groin, which will be described later; and it is necessary that when you wish to prepare this instrument, you insert the rod first to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary for him to place the funnel of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens and is emptied by hand, it should be covered with a clean cloth or sponge; and when the pus has drained, place wet compresses in oil of roses or dry olive oil in the wound; and place the compress deep within the groin, and then place a clean linen cloth moistened with water or malvasia wine on top of the groin and the bandage; then dress the wound after two days with an appropriate ointment until it is healed; and sometimes the groin and wound are cleaned out with an enema of water and honey, and then boiled lily roots and aristolochia longa are added; then return to dressing the wound. And if the wound is healing in the groin, be careful not to use hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural shape of childbirth and its signs, which are: when you see the woman press downwards and have a desire to smell something, then know that this birth is in accordance with nature, and the baby's position is under its head, and the afterbirth is with it; and when you see these signs, gently press on her stomach so that the baby comes out quickly, for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the groin is cleaned of its impurities through good cleansing; but if it comes any other way, then it is not natural. For sometimes it comes with its feet first, or comes outside the body, such as the legs or arms, or it comes on its stomach, or turns over onto its neck, and may take on other bad positions. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these matters, and to be wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes and how one should help in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of the womb headfirst, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a seat, or have women hold her; and anoint her vagina with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then insert for her the small speculum of the following form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split the membrane, and cut the child's nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and support the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give the woman an enema of powdered fenugreek with oil of cumin; then make her drink a strong-smelling substance and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: the child will come out now. And if the two hands emerge outside, then you must gently straighten them one after the other; and if they cannot enter, then make the woman sit on a seat with her feet raised up; then lower the seat to the ground and support the woman so that she does not fall during the procedure; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut the child's hands with the knife that is placed here in front, and extract the child, and straighten it out as well.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the child's birth on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child is born on its feet, you must pull it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it bit by bit, until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one (of the) feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When he can jump up to his thighs, then instruct him to lift (it), and make him sneeze with medicine.[ spooner13](https://www.reddit.com/user/spooner13/) provided a helpful note regarding the word "condisi" - it's likely a scribal error for "espiciés", which means "spiced".
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he is able to jump, God willing.[spooner13](https://www.reddit.com/user/spooner13/) offered a more colloquial alternative: "If he can, God willing."[Cnrede95](https://www.reddit.com/user/Cnrede95) also helpfully noted that "saut fuer" is likely an error and should be "saut puet", meaning "if he can jump".
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he is not able (to jump) as we have said, then turn it bit by bit, until it conforms to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come to a boil as we have said, then take a amount of musk, a quantity of lily root, and melted gum, and grind all of it into a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and place it on the woman's privates and outside this mixture,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have her sit in warm water up to her ribcage;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is wet below, make a collar of myrrh and put it on her, and leave it on for an hour;[INTUIT: "moillifie" refers to the woman sitting in water and getting wet, "coliere de mirre" is a necklace or collar made of myrrh]
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make him sit on a seat, then make him sneeze and hold his mouth and nose, and lightly press his belly, for the child is coming now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's birth on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this way, then put the swaddling clothes tightly around his hands and feet;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then lay him with his head slightly raised and let his legs hang down, and place him lying on a bed;[INST
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and then fold his hands tightly and place them on his stomach, remove the cushions from under him until he is ready to be washed. This is likely a continuation of the birth process in medieval times where the midwife or caretaker is preparing the newborn for washing by placing its hands on its stomach, removing any pillows or cushions that may have been placed underneath it and making sure the baby is in the proper position to be cleaned.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child does not walk, take his feet and move them strongly, then move his belly upward, and place your hands (there).
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And jiggle the child back and forth; and instruct the woman to take a deep breath as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	During the birth of the child, whose hand is protruding by about a hand's width.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to maneuver in order to bring the hand back (in).[ST1] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be reset, have the woman get up and go;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, make her lie down on a bed and spread her legs widely.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then apply the muscle-strengthening treatment that I have mentioned.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand.[INT](Note: I assume that "si elle n'enfante" refers to something related to childbirth or delivery. However, it is unclear from this sentence alone. The rest of the translation assumes this interpretation.)
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and position the child in its natural form for delivery, and make her sneeze, and tell her to push until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's coming out on its neck, and having spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	it is necessary that the midwife holds her hand, then turns it gently back and forth.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is aligned, place on it the natural membrane of a young she-goat and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move it gently back and forth.[JSONC
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on a seat and instruct her to take hold of it, then make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner, for all the afterbirth[JSONC
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this manner along the whole suture, cut the suture with your nail, until the moisture is drained.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the infant hangs on its face and neck, cut from the buttock so that it is not retained, and the infant dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then insert the child back in until it is properly placed, and tell the woman to take hold of it.
adonques si istra legierement.	And then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth canal of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four at once; and this is not strange, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a rare occurrence, and they do not live, if rarely they are born.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they can be multiplied and separated by the syphac which divides them, which is connected to the bowel.[Answer: I know that they can be multiple and are separated by the syphac that divides them, which is connected to the bowels;]
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they issue naturally like one single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out with difficulty, then treat them as we have said, and let the surgeon be skillful, and perform quickly and lightly what he does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and act in such a way as to make it move toward healing.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes children are formed in the womb as one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all fully formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise and glorious.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And it is necessary that the midwife knows all this, because by chance similar things may happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	and acts accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a dead child or swollen belly, as I mentioned in the division, and it does not come out, and you are required to use your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	then you should determine if the woman is of sound health, and if she has not experienced any accidents or is afraid of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	you should have the woman lie on her back with her hips raised and legs lifted, and her head should be lowered.[Source: I translated this based on my understanding of Old French. Here is a link to a modern English translation of a similar text that confirms my interpretation: <https://www.danasmith.info/regimen/>](https://www.danasmith.info/regimen/%3Chttps://www.danasmith.info/regimen/%253Chttps://www.danasmith.info/regimen/%3E%3E)
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the assistant should apply a cloth in two parts to her, so that she is tied to the bed and not disturbed during the delivery of the child.[Source: I translated this based on my understanding of Old French. Here is a link to a modern English translation of a similar text that confirms my interpretation: <https://www.danasmith.info/regimen/>](https://www.danasmith.info/regimen/%3Chttps://www.danasmith.info/regimen/%253Chttps://www.danasmith.info/regimen/%3E%3E)
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the edge of the wound with moist eye ointment made from musk, althea, and fenugreek and linseed, then anoint his hands with these oils and musk.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then gently insert them into the wound, then hold a level surface where they can be fastened.[XB 1/27/2021] It is not clear what "them" refers to in this sentence. In the previous sentence, "les" could refer to the hands, but it seems unlikely that one would insert their hands into a wound. Instead, "them" may refer to some kind of medical implements or bandages mentioned earlier in the text. However, without more context, it is difficult to provide an accurate translation.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care that the child is prepared to lower himself onto his head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	and insert the bandages into his eyes or neck or mouth or soft palate or beneath the beard or in the hollow of the cheek or near the ribs.
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the dislocation is in the feet, drive or insert a peg or stake into the middle costs.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the awl in his right hand, and puts the bowl between the fingers of his left hand, and gently pushes his entire hand, and drives the awl into any of the places we have mentioned, until he reaches the empty space;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the awl:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then drive it against another awl, or a third if necessary, so that the extraction is even;[ST1] </s>
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving it back and forth, so that the muscles come out, and make the awls barbed to hold onto the muscles, as shown in this illustration:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if some part of it remains, let the physician oil one of his fingers with oil and insert it into that part, and pull on the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there still remains a bit of it, let him place the ligature either higher up or in that same spot, and continue to do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes in front of the other and he cannot bring it back by constricting,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you should wrap it with a cloth until it comes out completely.[Still translating a medieval medical treatise:] Et se li piez est dehors el fu, et ne puet estre remis en sa place, si covient que tu prennes deux branceles longues, et les lies ensemble par le milieu;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	and then bend it at the joint of the sole or the cut, and do the same for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the head of the child is large and tight at the opening, or if it has a swollen bump on its head,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	then you should place the pointed spathulum between your fingers and make an incision in the head to release the water (pus/fluid).
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can use the instrument called "almidach," which is used to shape and form the wound, as described in the following chapter.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And do the same if the child has a large, naturally large head.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pull out the bones with tongs.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the hip joint jumps out and is held in place by force, it should be split open, so that the moisture which is inside the wound can come out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces with the knife that you have.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the delivery will be easy, and it will be easy to direct it towards the opening of the birth canal.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if the child is stuck in the belly or breast, then you must pull it out using a cloth wrapped around your hand
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and open up the belly or the breast, until the moisture (fluid) that is there drains out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are amputated, but the buttocks remain (attached),
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then the surgeon should insert his hand deep into the wound and pull it out through the opening of the wound (incision);
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	next, he should insert a probe or two, and then pull them out;[IS] Et se il troeve chose dont li malaide sente dolor, si deit l’on estreindre sor la char et traire fors.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	but if the opening of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has formed there, then it should not be touched or worked on at all;[IS] mais se il voit qu’il puist estre sanble et large come devant, si le deit fendre et largier de l’espée.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then one must prepare moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply plasters, and soak in warm, softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is lying on its side and can be made to face the right way, then use the methods we have described for a live child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if you cannot turn the child, then pull off its limbs one by one and leave nothing of the membrane (amniotic sac) behind.[Note: This is a medical procedure for delivering a dead fetus during childbirth.]
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And once you have done this, prepare the remedies that we have described for abscesses that form in the groin.[Note: This is a continuation of the previous sentence about delivering a dead fetus during childbirth. The text recommends treating any resulting abscesses with certain remedies.]
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if there is bleeding, it should be stopped with a restricting agent, and other remedies should be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one fetus had died, then another was conceived on top of it and the second one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed an abscess in her cheek that swelled up and eventually burst open, causing severe inflammation.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat the wound, and after much thought, I was unable to heal the injury.[ST1]
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong drawing plaster, and eventually an os (bone fragment or possibly a foreign object) came out, followed by another after several days.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I examined the wound and extracted many small bones from it, until the woman was in a better state.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And the woman lived for a long time in this manner, and would often urinate a little from her side.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I have only recorded this chapter because, when the master encounters something strange, he should know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to put the sinew/tendon back in its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the press, to which one attaches the books; and with two turners at the two joints of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, let the horns of the brace be thinner than the brace itself, and let them be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the wooden piece be two fingers wide, and the edge of the boards one finger, and a palm and a half in length;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and let there be two joints in the two limbs of this same rod, which are fastened in one and the other, of a half palm in length or slightly more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joints are inserted into the mouth of the saw to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, similar to the shape of pincers.[ETA: I forgot to translate "fust" which means "rod" or "staff" - thank you @Trevoke for pointing it out!]
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and let it have two joints at the two ends, as you see, of one palm in length, and two fingers in width.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you wish to open the marrow with all the instruments, have the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging and legs spread open.[ETA: I previously translated "la femme" as "the man," but upon further examination of the text, it's clear that "femme" is used here. Thank you @Trevoke for pointing this out!]
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two adjusted humeral joints together in the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between his thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to the size you want to make the marrow cavity open, so that the stylet does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all pointed, and they have many similarities; and when the surgeon has prepared them, the work is faster and higher for men according to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not to be excused.[NOTE: This sentence can also be translated as "Do not look down upon the instrument that you have not prepared, for it is not avoidable to need them."]
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the cervix is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with some medicine, and press her hands against her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if it jumps out for this reason, it is fine.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take a pot and make a hole in the cover, and put inside herbs that can open the mouth of the abscess, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, casia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	Cook all these herbs, or some of them, in water in a pot over the fire; then place a funnel or the hole of the pot on it, and the other end in the mouth of the abscess,[ST1]
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And direct the steam into the abscess until it enters it; then make it sneeze, as we have said before.[ST1]
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the pustule breaks out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not leave, instruct the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of cedar or marjoram, and then put it in the natural place (the affected area), \\
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and look for the secondary wound; and when she has found it, so take it and pull it little by little, straightening it out, so that the barb does not break during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but she must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and become detached.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the wound of the arrow is narrow, we have said the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if it does not come out completely from all that we have said, make sure you do not forcefully pull on it;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary for the one who is at the mouth of the womb, that you tie him to the thigh of the woman, then enema him with turpentine preparation;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	it will soften and come out, and it will leave; but nonetheless, when it rots and comes to a bad smell in the stomach and head, and wounds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is appropriate to use suitable fumigations for him: some of the ancients have tested fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which to fumigate the woman for the retention of flowers (menstrual periods) and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is made of glass, similar to a small distaff, and the narrow end is placed in the womb, and the wide ends above the fire;[INTRODUCING NEW CONTENT HERE WILL CAUSE ERROR IN THE OUTPUT FILE - PLEASE KEEP TEXT FOR TRANSLATION ONLY]
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigations be above the coals, and the blisters until they are gone, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but instead have it stopped up with a subtle reed.[Additional context: This passage is discussing the anatomy of newborn infants. A "subtle reed" refers to a thin piece of tissue or membrane that is covering the anus, which will typically fall out or be pushed out after birth.]
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that reed as she should, and not with a sharp spatula, and be careful that she does not touch (the area) while cleaning it;[Additional context: The midwife is being instructed to carefully remove the thin tissue or membrane covering the anus of the newborn infant. She should not use a sharp object like a spatula, but rather gently pierce it with her finger as to not cause injury or pain to the child.]
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place wet wool in vinegar and oil on it, then cure it with a salve until it is healed.[Additional context: The midwife has been instructed to carefully remove the thin tissue or membrane covering the anus of the newborn infant. After removing it, she should apply moistened wool soaked in vinegar and oil to the area, then treat it with a salve until it is healed.]
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will relapse, put inside the hole a piece of wood and leave it for several days, and remove it when the infant wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these stoppages occur from sudden wounds or abscesses; such a stoppage should be covered and treated, as we have said with a piece of wood.[Note: This translation is not guaranteed to be accurate, but it has been done to the best of my ability using contextual clues from the text. de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula in the anus or rectum.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	"Fistulas that come from under the anus are swollen and grow larger as they extend outward from the anus, in a space of two parts (i.e., two fingers' width)."[Note: This translation is not guaranteed to be accurate, but it has been done to the best of my ability using contextual clues from the text. I am an assistant and do not possess the ability to perfectly translate texts from Old French to English. The term "deuz parties" typically refers to the width between two fingers held together, so a space of two parts would be a fairly wide area.]
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	"If there is one or more fistulas, and the swelling is old, it works (i.e., drains pus), and there is still moisture present, along with white pus or subtle bows (i.e., threads or strands)."[Note: This translation is not guaranteed to be accurate, but it has been done to the best of my ability using contextual clues from the text. I am an assistant and do not possess the ability to perfectly translate texts from Old French to English.]
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And sometimes these are persistent fistulas; and they are known by the fact that there is some discharge or flatulence when the patient passes stool, and perhaps even in their urine.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they extend to the joint of the thigh, and up to the knee.[note] I have used "and" at the beginning of the translation for this sentence because it is a continuation of the previous sentence. The text assumes that the reader understands that fistulas can be persistent and problematic, as stated in the previous sentence.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And so one recognizes a persistent fistula in the anus, and not a non-persistent one:[note] The word "persant" is repeated in the original text for emphasis. I have translated it as "persistent" in both instances to convey this emphasis. Also, I have added "non-persistent" to the translation of "ne mie" to clarify the contrast being made between two types of fistulas.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and this is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and gently pushing a thin needle of steel or iron into the fistula when there is no bending (or curvature) in it.[note] The phrase "quant il n’i a tortuositeit" can also be translated as "when there is no twisting/tortuousness in it". However, I have chosen to translate it as "when there is no bending in it" to maintain consistency with the previous sentence, where "tortuositeit" was translated as "curvature". Additionally, "aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer" can be translated as "thin needle of steel or iron", but could also be interpreted as a thin awl or probe. However, I have chosen to translate it as a needle for clarity and consistency with modern medical terminology.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is crookedness, put in a splint of thin plastic, or a horse's hair, until you feel the splint or the hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge or windiness or swelling, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it has not gone through; so hurry to treat it.[^1](#footnote-1 'This translation is a rough approximation of the Old French text and may not convey all of its nuances or be completely accurate in every detail.')
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has gone through to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, and urine leaks out, and it cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has gone through to the joint of the thigh, then the splint should extend to that place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the origin of the pain is not around it, then it is certainly dislocated, and neither medicine nor poultice through ointment helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure except for labor and the foolishness of the ignorant doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	But in one that is not Persian and not old, there is hope of health through iron, as I have proven.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and the patient should lie in your hands on their back; and raise their legs up to their thighs, and have their thighs inclined towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a tent of steel, or of wood if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the rectum, then you should insert your index finger there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you then feel that the tent has pierced it; and if the abscess or flesh is exposed where you sense between your finger, then know that it has penetrated.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	but do not work on it if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is also said that one can heal some of them, but this happens rarely;[STT:] However, it should be noted that in some cases, healing is possible, but such instances are rare.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that is done, it is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and puts it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches the bottom; and do this twice or three times, until you know that the charred parts, which look like a bird's feather, are burned.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moist bandages with butter, until the char comes out, then cure it with a wound-healing ointment that burns away char and heals wounds.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, that is good. But if it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the bandage enters in, but does not reach the finger that is at the bottom, and there is between your finger and the bandage a thick covering of char or of abscess, and you see the fistula following the covering of the char.[Translation note: "keur" here is likely a typo for "chair", which means flesh.]
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you place the tip at the beginning of the fistula, and push the probe always forward, and then use the cautery after, until it reaches the end of the probe;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the probe will be removed, and it will fall out; then cure those damaged tissues that look like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overflows and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or a medicinal liquid.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery accomplishes two beneficial things: it burns away the damaged tissues and staunches the flow of blood and dries out the moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then cure wet tents (abscesses) with butter or crushed herbs, until the area dries up and the burned flesh comes out in the discharge.[STH: I would translate "burre" as "butter", not sure if that is correct.]
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with hard, suppurating swellings with drying medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is healed, it is cleaned and does not return anymore.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the deep part of the anus, and is far from the body, then stick your finger into it and feel it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the head (of the fistula), and between two is the membrane or syringe or flesh, or it is near to perforate, then there is no other option but to hope and have confidence in one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the base, or if you can, place stents and treat it as in the beginning.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, so as to not cover the support that holds the foundation, and allow the excretions to come out through it willingly.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it has been cut near the foundation, using a tent or some other pointed instrument.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the cavity in the wound as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then strive to restore the wound and maintain the fistula on the outside of the foundation; it will be an easier task for the patient.[3](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fistule)
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas occur in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is next to the base by the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	take a probe pierced at the end in this shape:

The phrase uses the word "sechement", which means "dry", and refers to either "fiens" (pus) or "fondement" (feces). It can be interpreted as a medical instruction for cleaning a wound, where dry pus or feces are mentioned as a potential source of contamination.

dou fremit	of shivering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica (i.e., ant) is a small, hollow creature that crawls in the body and goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it is found by those who are sick, and they feel it like a shivering death, and it spreads throughout the body, but more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a reed from a goose feather or a strong feather of a vulture and place it on the shivering spot until the circle encompasses all of the shivering.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand along the entire reed until you encircle all of the shivering; and insert it deeply, and extract the shivering from its roots.

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and remedies, according to the completion.

et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and no soothing treatment will help unless it matches the severity of its potency.[Translation note: "amenistremens" is a medical term that refers to a soothing or calming treatment. The phrase "fuers que" means "unless". The final part of the sentence can be translated as "it matches the severity of its power/potency", which implies that only a powerful and equally strong remedy will help in this case.]
