Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this is more likely to happen in those who have moist bones in their head, such as the head of a child.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens with all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated, as such; and I will speak of them later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the withdrawal (symptoms) on them, and through examination by probing, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top (of the break).
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hairline fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is exposed and one rubs against it, the fracture becomes blackened.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, be aware of the patient's condition, and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, fever, eyes coming out and turning red, and other similar conditions in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see frightening symptoms and hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month, when you are able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupt and the complications that we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you must cut open the injured part in this way: take hold of the head of the wounded person and expose the bone as much as you can, in the shape of the wound as gently as possible.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flows when the bone is exposed or an abscess occurs, you should use what is necessary and fill the space around the bone with cloths soaked in rose oil.[ST1]
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and you are certain that there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone in one of two ways: the first method is to make a narrow incision in front, and here is its shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then insert another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of steel; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and difficult to penetrate, then you should cut around it, so that you administer cuts with trephines, not so deep that they go beyond the bone of the skull; and above the tip there should be a ridge or a circle that does not allow the tip to go beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that each one comes into place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have trephines for all parts of the head; and this is the form of the three kinds of trephines.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for cutting around the bone are that you place a trephine on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the trephine to another spot nearby and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with incisors, doing this as delicately and lightly as you can, so that you extract the bone with your hand or with one of the instruments you have such as pliers, forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, then it is necessary to smooth the sharpness that remains from the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be more slender and thinner than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if any small bones or splinters remain, gently remove them with an instrument; then heal the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he highly praises it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a portion of the bone where the break is clearly visible. Once you have exposed that area, place the round-ended head of this scalpel beneath it, as shown in the following shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut all the way through on one side, but rather make two shallow cuts so that the knife faces the bone. Then gently tap with a small mallet to break the bone completely around, making sure not to damage the tissue underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is dislocated to the bone, gently detach it, for it can be easily removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the flesh, but is only chopped at the top with small pieces present, then you must smooth over that roughness and remove the splinters with a sharp razor, of which you should have various quantities to accommodate each situation as needed, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use large razors, then finer ones, and do not stop doing so until it is smooth.[ Anthology of Middle English Literature p. 146]
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other precise haircutting and fine fracture cases, one must adapt according to its orientation; this is not an easy task even for those who have devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the abscess is uncovered, you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another doubled cloth, of two layers or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another ligament on top, and don't tighten it too much, just enough to hold the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down, then loosen it and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetches flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and continue to apply painless medicine;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and make sure the wound stays clean, not allowing any residue or pus to accumulate, for if pus accumulates on the cloth on the head, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; for when you place something painful on the abscess, it causes necrosis.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take notice, if any bad accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no improvement comes from the medicine applied, unless it has such power, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in grease, wet one bandage, and place it on the shovelful (of medicine).
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with methods of healing until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone, for they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only swells or twists, and then heals.[translated by me]
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should push your little finger or the narrow part of the nose and place the break inside your index finger and thumb, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the knee, and the swelling cannot reach its place, then you must make it even with the end of a fairly large stick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, then do similarly, and hurry to set it on the first day, if you are able;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then attach splints made of linen cloth to the end of the shin if the fracture is in one piece.[*]
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should attach another one on the other side if there is a fracture there, and let the splints be thick enough to fill the openings of the shin.[*]
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that one must wet the splints with butter and change them every day. I do not think that this is a good idea, but it seems to me that they should be moistened with egg white and powdered mallow; then leave the splint in place until the bone is healed and the cartilage has hardened.[*]
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose pens are put in place of tenting, and then a soft cloth is wrapped around, and the breaker holds it, and the patient blows through it; do what you will.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses or pustules come on the nose while you are working, put on cerate or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a bag of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses or pustules do not come, put an emplaster on the outside, made of chamomile flour, and powdered incense, concocted with egg white, then place light swabs on top, but do not bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nose is small and it is broken into many pieces, then extract it with the appropriate instruments, then sew up the opening, and cure it of things causing bad flesh and blood, such as concocted plasters and ointments suitable for that.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then cure it with compresses, and put in splints of wood until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken underneath and there is no wound on the outside, and the fracture is only on the inside without breaking through, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, then insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture inward, and align it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two parts, then it is necessary to administer extension of both parts until they are even.[Notes:
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a breaking, then bind them with a gold or silver filament or silk, then place a heated plaster on the broken jawbone, and place on it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large, well-made star, or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide to the jaw, and tie it to the head as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and feed them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, then loosen it on the third day and realign what has shifted; and place a plaster on top, made from flour mill powder with plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the heated plaster; and place a light linen cloth on top of the plaster, and if the plaster hardens and the patient's condition does not worsen, leave it on until healed; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed from it; then carefully remove it with the appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as necessary.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all those pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound if it is large, and apply suitable ointments to it until the flesh heals.
de la forcele	The context of the previous sentences suggests that "de la forcele" might be a part of a medical instrument used for removing foreign objects or debris from a wound. However, without additional context, it is difficult to provide an accurate translation of "de la forcele". Here are some possible translations:
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times before, towards the shoulder, and the breaks are of three kinds: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and there are fragments, and this is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, one of whom holds the instrument with which the forceps are broken; and the other stretches out the neck towards the side; then place the break evenly between your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place below the patient's shoulder a round pillow of cloth or wool, and make it as thick as necessary; stretch and lift the strap, and pull the sphere with your hand, so that you align the break, as is required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the strap outward because it goes too deep, have the patient lie flat on their backside, place a medium-sized pillow under their shoulder, and have the assistant push the shoulder downward until the bone of the strap is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the break with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, make an incision; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, cut one of the incisions that you made, but place this instrument underneath the strap to protect the suture.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should look like a spoon, but not be sharp-edged, and be of appropriate width according to the size of the bone and the magnitude of the task; and it should have two openings, one wide and one narrow, similar to the opening of the wound you made when you pulled out the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, then bandage the wound with strips of cloth and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses should come, wet one cloth in rose oil, vinegar, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is to place poultice of mill powder and egg white on the bone, then put light wicks on top, and place a stick underneath if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then put a double cloth on the wicks and poultice; then take a thin strip of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage is hanging down;[ST1]
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the strip on the fracture, then turn the bandage around the neck and under the healthy saddle and under the patient's saddle; and massage each part, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture properly, and it is clear that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the binding loosens, then tighten it again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under their shoulder blade to lift the armpit; this will lighten the fracture through the alignment of the shoulder, or you can tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an accident occurs, until 20 days have passed.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the poultice if necessary, and bind it in this way until they are healed; and it is healed for most people in 28 days, and sooner for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates without being noticed, except through touch; therefore, treat it according to the type of fracture, and reset it in its natural position in every way possible; then place on the area powdered flour with a lot of egg white, and light bandages, and put on a double cloth; then place a wide and thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate in any part of the shoulder, fill those areas with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then bind it firmly with a large bandage so that the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it softens, tighten it again, and adjust the plate if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days has passed, untie it, but be careful, because it is not an easy thing for the bone to come out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breaking of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the breaking (fracture) of the arm.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks near the joint. And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of blood flow, quickly, and perhaps they vomit blood, and the fracture can be seen clearly in the broken bone, and one can tell easily.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration (treatment) is that the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then you press the shoulders together and bring the ribs of the two sides together with your hands, gently adjusting them equally as much as possible so that the shape of the bone is correct. Then you apply poultices and compresses made of salt or some other light wood over the fracture, and wrap it in a bandage, tying it securely to the broken bone so that it does not move; and tie the bandage around their back, tightening it appropriately, and check frequently to make sure it has not loosened. If it becomes loose due to corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, remove the poultice, and treat what has come there in accordance with medical practices; then reapply the poultice and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes about in heavy blows to the back and the chest, and they do not bend further because they are slippery; and this can be easily detected by examining the wounds.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the setting of the broken ribs is to align the break as it should be. Then apply a poultice and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of ribs leans inward, then the patient feels great pain and shortness of breath, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lining; and there is sharp pain in the side, and immediate vomiting of blood, which is a serious condition. The ancients have employed much skill in treating this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one must administer food which causes the belly to swell in order to push the break outward.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come to one.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come to a boil, lance them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that cupping glasses should be applied to the affected area, in order to draw out the impurities strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cups will attract superfluidities to the weakened area due to their disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that the area should be covered with a cloth soaked in warm oil, and tents (i.e., bandages or compresses) should be placed between the ribs to hold the wound evenly around, then treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pointing through the skin, and the patient is fearful, then a cut should be made above the broken rib, and an instrument placed underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone should be cut and gently removed, and then the two edges of the wound, if they are large, should be sewn up and treated with poultices until it heals. And if abscesses appear, then place wet bandages soaked in rose oil on top, and on the side; and treat the side for what is necessary for the abscess, and lie down on the side where it is, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there comes a break in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, see if you notice their hands are softened, swollen, and without feeling, and that they cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. You should know that in many cases this means death, but if they can move them and feel well when pressed and poked, then the joints of the bone are safe, and the patient will be healed if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, look to see if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms present in the hands, and on the back there is a swelling without desire to be egested; and when it is turned onto its stomach, there is still egestion without desire. And when it is turned onto its back and it wants to move, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, the condition is easier to deal with.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	The treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess on the spine, apply heated oil of roses or egg yolk until it calms down; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters and bind it with a bandage, ordering the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislodged, it is necessary to cover the wound with linen; remove the bone and stitch up the two lips of the wound if it is large; apply a healing ointment until it heals. If the head of the bone is broken (called "head of the cow"), insert your left hand into the wound and push the bone back in place as far as you can, then apply a plaster and bandage if necessary. Restrain the area and if there are any dislodged bones, remove them and clean the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight reduction in size at the top; and it bends long, and tilts to the side, and comes to the patient pain and swelling at the site of the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand over the break, so that you are above the breaker; and know what the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the top, then make the break even, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it tilts to the inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that break can be prepared for you.[IT] Et se il avient que li os sunt desjoinctz ou par chu de hors ou par chu dedens, si li fai cheoir sus le dos ou sur un baston qui soit a ses piez; et si les remet ensemble dou sovent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the poultice, then place a wooden or iron bar on top of it and tighten the breaker so that it does not move; and apply medication under the ribs until the ligaments are aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we mentioned before; then return to treatment and bind it as is appropriate, unless there is any adverse event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	on the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one that is between the neck and the arm, and if it is dislocated, it should be treated in one of two ways: the first way is to take a rod of medium thickness, shaped like this:[This sentence contains some instructions for shaping a rod, but I'll need more context or an illustration to accurately translate that part.]
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the shoulder joint with two ligaments and fasten them upwards, and lay the patient on a seat; then throw their broken arm over the rod until it reaches the armpit and forms a bow shape around the rod; then suspend it from some heavy weight or have the minister stretch it downwards; then place the surgeon's hands together over the break, holding them in that position until the bones return to where they should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is as follows: lay the patient face down on a support, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants, one of whom should hold what is above the break with his hands, and the other below, at every ligament, and each extend it in its direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tighten one ligament above and below the break, and have each of the assistants extend it in its direction. And if the break is near the shoulder joint, then you must place one ligament in the middle beneath the armpit, and another towards the side, beneath the break; and do the same if the break is towards the side. Then align the break as it should be, and tighten it if there is no danger of abscesses.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does occur, then do not tighten it for seven days and instead place a linen cloth soaked in vinegar and rose oil on the break until the abscess subsides; then tighten it. The method of tightening is as follows: apply the poultice to the break, then place the arm on a support, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and place the bandage, and tighten it on the arm and the support so that the arm remains in place, unless something prevents it, or if the bones are not aligned.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you suspect that the bones are not aligned, then use a device called an "estel," and place above the break a wider and stronger estel than the others, with a space of one finger between each estel, and each estel should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side. Then tighten it over the estels as I described at the beginning of this chapter on the break, first tightly and then less so as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you reset the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine every three days if there is itching, inflammation, or coming of fluid to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. If that is the case, loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not unbind it before three or more days have passed, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool beneath the affected area, and check every hour of the day and night if the shape of the broken member has changed or if the bindings have loosened; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give the patient the food that we mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially light; and when they begin to recover, make it richer. And it is customary for the affected area and leg to be recovered in 40 days in total; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to direct the place. And if the stricture is bad and swollen, then delay unbinding for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Here is the translation of the text with added context:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "foscile" (humerus), of which one is small, and it is the one that follows the armpit; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small ribs are broken, the restoration and healing is easy, and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when they are broken together. If it is only the small rib that is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large ribs, then they must be stretched more forcefully; and they should be laid out over a cushion, and the patient's arm should be raised higher than the other, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and the patient should be crosswise on top of it, with a cushion before them that the patient can bear without discomfort. Then the assistant should extend the patient's arm below at the level of their hand, or with a bandage, and another assistant should do the same above. And then the surgeon should align it evenly, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is in pieces, then each piece should be put in its place, and if there is any piece that is torn and pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then saw through it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of this in a separate chapter; then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the healing process, boils occur, then apply a piece of linen soaked in a mixture of rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and gently place another linen cloth on top until the boils subside. Then remove the wax, and apply the plaster made of powder from the mill with plenty of egg, then put on the stylets, and let the one from the breakage be stronger and a bit larger than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches in multiple arrangements: either the breakage be in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more above the breakage than any other part, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths above the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And wrap the member and the bandage after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any mishap occurs to the member, such as itching that comes upon the member, then it is necessary to rinse the member with warm water until the itching subsides; and do not let the member rest too tightly. Then resume binding, and if the bandage is weakened and the bones disjointed, and similar things, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the circulation does not come to the member because it is too tight, then you should loosen it slightly and leave it like that for a few days until the circulation returns, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things that we have mentioned do not come to pass for the patient, then do not unbind it until after twenty days or thereabouts. Then let him clasp his hands behind his neck, and let his neck be even, and watch for movement and loosening, and let him sleep on his back; and know that this breakage is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps even in twenty days, depending on the mixtures and complexions of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks often occur at the back of the hand and the knuckles of the fingers, and they tend to bend many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should sit cross-legged and face straight ahead; then place their hand on a spread-out cloth, and have the assistant straighten out the broken bones and align them evenly until they are properly joined; and apply a poultice and bandages, unless abscesses form, then place a piece of wood according to the size of the wound; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outer edge around the stomach of the palm, then make a ball of cloth and command the patient to squeeze it with their broken hand; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the piece of wood be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, then place a piece of wood on top and another underneath in the palm of the hand, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and fasten the binding between the fingers.[STHAPHANUS: I can't seem to find any more text to translate. Is there anything else you would like me to do?
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the bone setter comes to one of our fingers, if it is crooked, make it straight as it should be; and hold it in place with the sole (of your hand), and if you see fit, place a small, straight stake to lift up the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index finger or one of the others, make it straight and bind it to the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together so they are immobile, or place a stake on it like a splint; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is evident when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is to tie one ligature above the fracture, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each of the assistants extends their ligature to their equal part; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the hip's root, let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture. And likewise if it is near the knee, and then let the ligament be next to the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the doctor place the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bandage, if pus does not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it settle down, then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap around the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, leaving the excess; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg next to the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come up; then wrap around the leg and the thigh the bandage, then put on the fracture a stylet, and one stylet on the bone of the leg; then apply soft cloths on the gap between the leg and the thigh to make equal the tightening, then begin to tie strongly three or four turns above the fracture; and when it goes above the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and bind them with three stitches that are above, then go down below to the end of the thread, so that you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, if no abscess or swelling or any similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is any abscess or swelling, untie it and treat what appears as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of the bone that protrude, they must be cut off if possible; and if not, the wound must be opened, and the fragments removed; and cure it as we have said, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and arm; however, with this kind of restoration, the patient is not made completely better.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin by the knee.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the groin by the knee there are few breaks, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and it happens with all wounds, whether they have wounds or not, and this can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one sets even what is dislocated at its joints, until it can be moved; then applies the poultice, and places a round bandage if needed, and binds it as required, then takes care of all the considerations that we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar things; and for each symptom does what is necessary, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Here comes the translation of the given sentence with the added context:
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by its proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it has all other breaks just as it does in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is entirely similar.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, set them straight again.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bones are broken, there is great pain and it is visible; and set them right underneath. Then provide extension and align it evenly, and tie the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is severe and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and support it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two straps of wood that encircle the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap around it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it evenly in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and this is good. And some apply a splint along the length of the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly in fractures where there is an open wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is any redness, swelling, or other symptom; and treat it until it has healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of bones of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but at the bones of the foot there can be a fracture and at the joints, and it only happens that they become dislocated in multiple ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see these bones protruding over one another, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are raised, press hard until they return to their places, then apply a plaster and bandages. Place a small board with two flat sides under the belly of the foot, then bind it to the foot appropriately after wrapping cloth around it and any other necessary items.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding because you will find that the bones are even, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; place a splint on the broken toe that is in proportion to the length of the toe and slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned and bind it appropriately. If there are two or three, or more, broken toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and have the end of the board come out from under the belly of the foot so that it supports it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone (os du poignet)
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's arm is fractured, make her sit with her arm extended, then lean her back and support her from behind; fill the hollow of her elbow with cotton, as thick as a finger; then lift her up straightening her arm, and let the cotton come out until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and let the bone come together with the finger; when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and replace it after she finishes; do this for seven or eight days: the fracture will be healed. And if you wish, take a bladder of a sheep, attach a cane to its opening, insert the entire bladder into her wound; blow strongly into the cane until the bladder is filled inside: the nature (body) will return and the fracture will heal; then fill it with cotton and leave it for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the arm, whether it be a man or a woman, is fractured, then restore it as we have said in the treatment of leg bones; and such fractures are not hidden to those who apply their attention and skill, and attend my book. For the fracture indicates clearly the right way to restoration, so pay close attention:
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis in it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the drainages which we have mentioned testify to it.[Note: "sainies" refers to the discharge or drainage from the wound]
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy (clean, free from infection), then apply vitriol to it (if you have none other thing), and then begin to reduce (set) the fracture in that same hour, or on that day, unless an abscess forms.[Note: "restainche" means to cauterize; Vitriol is a category of mineral salts, particularly those of sulfuric acid][Additional note: "reducer/reduce" is a term used for setting bones back into their normal position]
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess (localized collection of pus) forms there, then postpone the reduction (setting) for nine days until the abscess is healed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about a harmful occurrence.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin, it is necessary to put it back in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to put it equally with your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, having 7 or 8 inches in length, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare 3 or 4 of them, depending on what is needed in each bone-breaking treatment; and let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the member while working, and let it be sharp at the front, and thick from the middle towards the end, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "palancelle", for which the curved head should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it once, until it returns to its place, and let them be aligned one against the other. And if the fracture is small, and the instrument cannot hold the bone properly, then you must cut the end of the bone, so that the instrument has enough power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as an osteotome or a chisel, to your ability; then smooth out the roughness and small shards that remain in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.
