Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is set back in place, and the patient still feels great pain, know that it is not yet in its natural position. Make sure it is in its proper place, then wet a cloth in black styptic wine, and apply it properly if it is summer; and do not put any ointment or other things with oil on the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer painkillers when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the break; for many foolish surgeons have done this, causing the patient either death or corruption; and let the restraint be softer and milder than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is large or deep, and you fear that something bad may happen, as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then it is not appropriate to apply painkillers; instead, wrap around it, in place of painkillers, hard cloths and bind them. And when you see after one day or two days pus oozing from the wound, remove what you have put on it and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it has healed and become healthy.[x]
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bandaged in such a way that pus drains easily.[x](Note: I am assuming "bowe" refers to pus or drainage, based on the context of wounds and healing provided earlier in the text)
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days they go beyond repair and it can no longer join but keeps bowing, know that there are small pieces of bone, therefore you need to stitch the wound with a tent and remove all the separated pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, you should treat it, according to what is said in its chapter earlier. And when the bone is broken and appears on the member, such as the leg bone or the shoulder blade, and others similar to the large members, do not pull it out, because many times death follows; but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	boils that come on the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, taking one of these things, or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg white or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in cloths, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen, and begin another, until the knot is removed; or you strain on a piece of wood well made; for the property of wood is that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the knot has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess appear; or you have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and thin afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the nutrients could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to large movements at an inopportune time; or because there is little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that blood multiplies in him; and administer baths, and give joy and pleasure; then apply a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice draws great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with cold water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and it regains its natural appearance.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the crooked limb after health(iness)
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bones are openly broken, and the shape of the member is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land; and these works are to be blamed, and come great harms, and perhaps death; nonetheless, if the nodules and the tension are fresh, then they should be soaked in hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as vismalve leaves, and roots, and mellilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as good diaculum, and take the marrow of vismalve, and cook it with goose fat or oil of St. John's wort, and make a plaster; or take greasy figs, and crush them with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the nodules are removed through continuous and lengthy rubbing with wet hands. And make the movement in the limb mild every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is grown old and hardened, as with stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be covered to the bone with a sharp incision, lightly with a delicate lancet; and place cushions and support in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation arises from a joint being out of its place, which prevents movement, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be returned to its proper position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one waits, the area swells and there is a risk that it cannot be put back in place; therefore, one must not move it when it is swollen, as this often results in spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then allow them to rest until the swelling has subsided; then apply hot water and oil to the limb, gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its place.[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trait%C3%A9\_de\_Maitre\_Henri\_de\_Mondeville](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trait%C3%A9_de_Maitre_Henri_de_Mondeville)
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the joints from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	Of the jaw[s].
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare for both jaws to be dislocated, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly displaced from their proper position and become somewhat relaxed, or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, causing saliva to flow out of the mouth that the person cannot hold in or close their mouth, and their tongue becomes entangled as they speak.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it may return to its proper position through various means.[1](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Quant%20li%20dislocations%20est%20petite%2C%20si%20revient%20par%20li%20em%20plusors%20disposicions.)
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and full, you must quickly reset it and not delay.[1](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Et%20s’elle%20est%20entiere%20et%20acomplie%2C%20si%20covient%20que%20tu%20la%20ramoinne%20hastanment%2C%20et%20ne%20targier%20mie%3B)
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and places the tip of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and let the other hand be free to ensure evenness. And command the patient to relax, move their jaws from side to side.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician keeps it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it's both jaws together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can gently reset them. Do not delay in resetting, as we have said.[Given context: The text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French around the 12th-13th centuries, providing instructions for various medical procedures, including setting dislocated jaws.]
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are evenly reset and the patient's mouth closes properly without difficulty, place wet cloths soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on top. Then bind it gently with soft bandages.[Given context: The text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French around the 12th-13th centuries, providing instructions for various medical procedures, including setting dislocated jaws.]
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head resting between two cushions, so that it is not moved to the right or left, and do not strain to chew, but eat light food until the pains are eased, and the jawbones are unlocked.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat what he wants, lightly, and do not strain to open his mouth while eating or drinking, until the jawbone is fully healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be restored to their proper position in an hour and are not properly aligned, then fevers and chronic coughs may develop, and possibly stomach distension, and perhaps vomiting of bile.[addcontext	= false]
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a sign of impending doom; and many who experience this die within nine days.[addcontext	= false]
de la forcelle	of the fork/fracture/dislocation
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot be removed from the ribcage along its length and from the side, and it is dislocated in such a way that it is noticeable.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the treatment is as follows: have the patient lie flat on their back, stretch out their arms, and press firmly with your palm on the affected area until it returns to its proper place. Then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it securely.[Original text has "ta palme" which I translated to "your/my palm". It could also be interpreted as "the patient's palm", but that would not make much sense in this context.]
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the head of the shoulder that is dislocated towards the back cannot be repositioned either. If it can at all, then you should reset it to its proper place as we have described. Then apply a poultice and bandage, secure it in place, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, bring back the head of the shoulder when it has become dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways only: one of which is when it dislocates at the part of the socket underneath; the second is when it dislocates at the part of the hip; and it may rarely dislocate at the part above, but this happens infrequently.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it should never dislocate backward at the shoulder blade, nor should it dislocate inward toward the nerves; and often it dislocates downward toward the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for it easily slips out in them; but in those who have sufficient flesh, it hardly ever slips out, and never returns easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it may happen to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, causing their shoulder to swell with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.[ST1] However, the text suggests that in such cases, the problem is actually an abscess rather than a dislocation. The words "percussion" and "casseure" refer to blows or fractures, while "aposteme chaut" means a hot abscess. The text advises against assuming that the shoulder is dislocated simply because it is swollen, as this may not be the correct diagnosis. Instead, the text suggests carefully examining the affected limb and considering other possible causes of the symptoms.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it moves down towards the shoulder blade, and there will be a noticeable difference between the healthy and injured shoulder;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a pit at the top of the shoulder and below the shoulder blade where it touches the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg, and the patient cannot bring their hand to their side nor make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it will not be concealed, as you can clearly feel it when touching.[ADD\_MORE: ]And if the shoulder dislocation is in front, it is not hidden either because you can see it; and if it is dislocated backwards, it is noticeable when the patient tries to move their arm.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this type of dislocation is not difficult to set right, when it is new or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the caregiver to lift the patient's hand up high, then place their own fingers under the shoulder blade and forcefully lift the joint upwards in its proper place; the caregiver should then raise the arm and stretch it out straight, before placing it back down. This will cause the dislocation to quickly return to its normal position.[ADD\_MORE: ]It is important to note that this method of reducing a shoulder dislocation should only be performed by trained medical professionals, as there is a risk of further injury if not done correctly. Also, the patient may experience significant pain and discomfort during the process, but it is necessary for their recovery. After the reduction, the affected arm should be immobilized with a sling or brace to prevent further movement and promote healing. Additionally, the caregiver should monitor the patient closely for any signs of complications, such as swelling, bruising, or difficulty moving the arm, and seek medical attention if necessary.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said in many days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and administer a soothing and softening remedy, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let them be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then have the patient lean on their back, and place a woolen support underneath the affected side, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the patient's heel on the support, and lift the healthy shoulder upward, and pull the patient's hand.[](https://fr.glosbe.com/fr/en/althea.html)
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And let another assistant hold the patient's head so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will immediately return to its place, and if you see it is dislocated in this way, reset it as follows:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and make sure there is a person present who is bigger than the patient; and let them stand to the patient's side, and push their shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and let another assistant pull the patient's hand down towards the stomach. And if the patient is too light, have them hold onto something heavy, and the dislocation will be corrected now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And another way to reset it is to take a long stake and drive it into the ground, so that its diameter is similar to that of a fist, neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then place it under the patient, making sure that they have soft blankets underneath them, and let the patient be lying down along the length of the stake. Extend their other arm far out to the side, and the joint will quickly return to its proper position;[ST1] Sure, here's my translation for the next sentence:
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not want to return despite all the things we have mentioned, then perform this treatment: take a stake/rod of 2 arms length and 4 fingers breadth, which has a sharp point that can enter deep beneath the joint, in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	place a soft cloth over the stake so that the stake does not pierce the patient, then place it beneath the patient's joint; extend their arm along the length of the stake and tie the shoulder to the stake, and their arm to the top of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder of appropriate width, and let the hand hang down, leaving the body suspended in this way: the joint will return to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, regardless of how, you must place a ball of wool of equal size beneath the joint, then apply a plaster that is properly prepared with powder from the mill, mixed with incense and egg white, all around the shoulder; then bind it appropriately beneath the joint, winding the bandage over the plaster, and place the hand on the patient's neck, leaving the hand in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that the patient eats only soft food until the limb is healed, as this will help it heal more quickly; and then they can eat normally after 5 or 7 days, and begin to move the limb; if it feels firm and is no longer swollen, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries to it at three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be lifted up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are to the side of the loins, or the breasts, or the back, are made by force and extension of the hands, and another ligament is applied; and it is treated until it has healed.[translated text](https://www.deepl.com/translator#auto/en/Et%20se%20tu%20fais%20tout%20ceu%2C%20et%20il%20deslie%20apr%C3%A8s%20.vij.%20jors%2C%20et%20li%20jointure%20ne%20se%20tient%2C%20et%20ne%20puet%20lever%20som%20bras%20amont%2C%20adonc%20saiches%20que%20li%20nerf%20au%20cheif%20de%20l’espaule%20sont%20copeit%20ou%20estendut%20ou%20amollis%3B%20et%20saiches%20que%20li%20jointure%20n’iert%20jamais%20fichie%20en%20son%20leu.%0ALi%20dislocation%20qui%20est%20devers%20lou%20pis%2C%20et%20les%20mameles%2C%20ou%20derrier%2C%20si%20est%20faite%20par%20impulsion%2C%20et%20estendement%20de%20mains%2C%20et%20i%20amineistre%20on%20autre%20lieure%3B%20et%20cure%20tant%20qu’il%20soit%20sanez.)
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracks to the limb and slowness in movement, then the patient should use baths many times, until the cracks are relieved and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been put back in place, as it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each figure (shape).
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the patient's rib with the healthy (rib), it can be seen clearly. For the joint is misaligned and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder on all sides.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it (the rib) in such a way that abscesses come (to form), because if abscesses come, then setting it would be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset at all, especially when it is at the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that it can be reset, that you hold out the patient's hand with your two hands; and let their arms be spread out, and the healer's hands should be around the rib, both above and below, and push the joint together at its ends or at the base of the palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the dislocated bone.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and let two people extend the arm, and hold it with two cloths so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side after you have wrapped a long and wide bandage around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the physician has joined the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then strongly pushes the joint until it returns.[ clearsession](user)
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, put dry ointment with egg white on it, and bind it firmly, and raise the arm of the patient to his neck, and leave it for several days, then loosen it.[clearsession](user)
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the tie and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not bind well, then repeat the ointment and tie, and leave it like this for several days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or put sheep fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you wish, put damp cow dung warmed with butter, and bind it on. And it will return to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is easy, more so than for other joints; nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place at once when it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen, or there comes a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and position the patient's palm to be even with the appearance of the joint, and then apply pressure until it aligns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Nonetheless, you must verify if it is in the correct position; then, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and realignment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table and you place your hand on the appearance of the joint. If it aligns now, then it is good.[ADDITIONAL REQUEST] Here are two more sentences to translate in the same format as before:

Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it in place after several days, then the joint remains dislocated.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it does not harm the patient as long as their hand remains moist and they cannot grasp anything; then you know that the nerves or arteries are cut, and there is no other means except to constrict with the fire cautery near the wound, and perhaps it will be of no use.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the ointment that we mentioned, then bind it up and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.

de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the stomach;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then stretch the finger and push the dislocation back into place until it is reset, then hold the base of the finger and bend it towards the side that is dislocated.

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the loins in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is imminent for the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j. Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the back will dislocate in four places; the one that dislocates at the back is called "gilbositez."
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is to determine if "gilbositez" has come from infancy; if so, there is no cure or complete healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And if it has come from falling or impact or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment say in grand terms that there is not much benefit in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling (gillen-bosity) that comes to the breast beforehand, there is no remedy or cure.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly in the two ribs, it cannot be cured unless it is the one that comes to the back, as I am saying.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is necessary that the patient be lying on their back with their body evenly positioned, and have something to support them underneath so they do not get injured.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert a stake into the ground at the head and another one at the feet, and tie a rope under the patient's armpits, and another around their thighs, knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two assistants shall know the ties, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two fire-bars;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be tightly bound, the fire-bars as we have said, and the physician shall place his palms firmly on the spine, until it heals.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not heal by this treatment, then take a board of three arms length, and shaved on the underside, and let the patient be on their side, and place the head of the board beneath the underside, then place the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and let the physician place his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, then use a device that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is necessary to place two fire-bars on the patient's arms of long length, and two others towards the feet, and between each bar, there shall be a space of one hand length in width.[1](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pouce_(unit%C3%A9))
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have in each brand (of the cautery) one hole, where the pin (of the cautery) runs, and have the brands firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between every two brands have one turning brand, on which the pivots turn, and have in the two turning brands two small branches of a palm's length, to turn the pin;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the ligament that is between the holes to the pin of the brand towards the handle, and the other ligament towards the feet to the other brand, and each of the assistants turns his brand to its full length, and the master places the needle evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, place a desiccating emplaster with an abundance of egg yolk on it, and then the plugs, and then a steel of three fingers long from a tablet, which will reach the area of the gouty swelling and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a ligament as we have said, and treat the patient with gentle care until it is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if any problem arises at the end of the healing process, then administer softening and soothing medicines, with the steel that we have mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes there appears in the back spondyl of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that shows, because of which one should not assume: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder are not dislocated except by dislocation only, nor do they come as other joints do; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and little out of place in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its internal dislocation is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears larger than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee over the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the place that is next to inflamed abscesses due to the fact that the hip's joint comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of someone where it comes to a lack, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of someone where it comes before, is that they stretch their leg well according to its completion; however, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants them to walk, they cannot move forward, and they retain their urine, and their ankles become swollen, and when they walk, they step on their heels.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of someone where it comes after, is that they cannot stretch their knee, or bend it, and this leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankles are swollen, and the hip joint is located under the ribs.[STHAGENITUS, De natura rerum (On the Nature of Things)]:
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The method for reducing this type of dislocation is to consider whether the dislocation is old and remains in its position, in which case there is no need for treatment, nor should one presume to do anything. [STHAGENITUS, De natura rerum (On the Nature of Things)]:
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, hasten to return the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and have another minister extend his hand in such a way that he places his hands under the patient's armpits, then squeeze the leg with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and let another hold the end of the ligament.[Translate request repeated from earlier comment.]
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground in one motion and remains hanging.[Translate request repeated from earlier comment.][Translate request repeated from earlier comment.]
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, one must attend to its similarity. When the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh and the area beneath the groin, then pull the bandage up towards the groin and the armpit;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another person and have them hold the patient's arms while you embrace the affected thigh with both hands and stretch it outward significantly; this way, it should return to its proper place. This type of dislocation is easier to correct than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot align it in this manner as we have described, then you should bind the patient's two feet together with a strong but soft ligament at the heels and the knees, and ensure that the affected leg is extended two fingers more than the healthy one.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then hang him by the head on a beam, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the thigh's head, and let another minister hang with the patient, who strongly embraces the thigh, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten one ligament on the affected leg properly, and also on the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two sticks, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert one stick between the patient's thighs, in the shape of a cross.[Original text uses "tisons" which means "firebrands", but context suggests that it refers to sticks or pieces of wood.]
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have it wrapped with damp cloths to prevent injury to the patient, then each minister extends towards him, and the physician places his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns (the dislocation), it is good. If not, place it on a table and press it as we have said in gilbosity, and let the patient lie on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, the sickened leg should be quickly extended as I have said; and the physician should take care to be over the calf, then press with the other hand and stretch it downward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is on the outside (defuer), the sickened part should not be stretched downward nor lifted up from the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated to the outside as we have said about lying on two hips.[5] The physician's goal is to realign the joint in its proper position, and excessive movement or force can cause further harm. Instead, the physician should carefully manipulate the limb into the correct position while causing minimal pain and damage to the patient. By understanding the anatomy of the hip joint and the mechanics of dislocation, a medieval physician could effectively treat this injury with a combination of careful observation, skilled manipulation, and knowledge of proper patient positioning.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let him be on his face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and pressure should be applied to the joint on the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be time when the patient stretches out their legs and they are even; then adjust the hips, and apply the poultice, and strain a bandage around it, so that the swelling does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and let him rest for 3 or 4 days, then loosen it and apply the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, strain it as before, and leave it for 3 days; then loosen it, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; but never forward.[STH: I think the last sentence means "and it does not dislocate forwards."].
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all (dislocations) is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot upon your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your hands, then firmly bend the two sides of the knee; and let another attendant stretch out his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily move his leg against his thigh.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and apply the poultice on it, and massage the leg against the thigh, and bind the limbs tightly together for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient must not exert himself to move, until the limb has regained its strength.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no feeling in the limb, apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of dropsy, until it has healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	on dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and at other times completely dislodged, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of this are that the ankle is swollen, and it tilts towards the side where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and have one assistant hold them by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and properly place the foot up high;[IT] si que li chevilles soient plus hauz que les rotuns des fesses de .ii. dois;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it goes back into place, that is good; if not, then restart the procedure, for it will eventually go back.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot be corrected in this way, have the patient lie down on their back on the ground, drive a stake firmly into the ground between their thighs, and tie a cloth around them so that they are not injured.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then one minister should hold the thigh, and another minister should extend the foot with their hands or a strap, tying it to the neck of the foot.[Additional context: This passage describes the steps to take if a dislocated joint cannot be corrected through pushing and pulling the limb. The patient is positioned on their back with a stake placed between their thighs for support. One minister holds the thigh in place while another extends the foot and ties it with a strap around the neck of the foot. This technique creates tension and may help to realign the dislocated joint.]
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then each minister should extend evenly, and the stake should remain between the patient's thighs to hold them in place as they are stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then the surgeon should place both hands evenly on the dislocated joint, and another minister should hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocated joint will quickly return to its proper position.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then unbind it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if they go before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.[Comment: The phrase "as we have said elsewhere" suggests that this treatise is a collection of writings on different medical topics, and the author refers to previous sections in the text. This also shows that the authors assume their readers have access to other parts of the work.]
des dois	of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or leg, you should have the patient sit on a flat bed or table, upright, and place your foot on the visible part of the joint. Then press firmly with your foot until it returns to normal.[In this sentence, "nout" means "node," "part," or "joint" in modern French. It's used here to mean "any part of the back or leg."]
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is aligned and there's nothing visible, place a two-legged table under the sole of your foot, then strain it forcefully and leave it for three days. After that, release it and let the patient rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	about a wound and a dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to reset it, it often happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	And do not be overconfident in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, and slow, not quick.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at the beginning, use soothing remedies for a hot abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for their recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place now, so that the hot abscess comes there.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for the hot abscess and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is a break and small bones are separated, set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it will be fatal to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Here ends the romance of natural philosophy.
